O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	Here is the translation:
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it has come to me in vision that I will complete it with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is forgotten in our region and is unknown throughout all, so the science is perished and decayed, and nothing remains except for the small descriptions in books of the ancients that the hands have moved.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this has come the error and vanity, and intentions are closed, and the science is estranged.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	Or it seems to me that I will bring it back to life together with the arrangement of this treatise according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and I will come together with the forms of instruments for cauterizing and other tools of work with the adjustment of declaration and preparation, as is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because for this reason no good masters of hands are found in our time, the art of medicine is estranged.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary for the one who undertakes this to ascend in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, so that he knows the proportions of members, and their forms and connections and separations, and has knowledge of bones and nerves and veins and the number of joints, and their movement and rest, and the location of their origin.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And therefore Hippocrates says that a name without a name is much, and with work is little; and the same thing is true in the art of hand.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We warn you in the introduction to this book that whoever is not familiar with the things said above, beware lest he fall into error and kill men; thus I have wished many times for those who undertake this science to abandon their ignorance and lack of experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa .i. apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I saw a foolish surgeon who cut open an abscess of scrofula or the neck of a woman, and cut the arteries of the neck; therefore so much blood issued forth that the woman fell dead between his hands.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens .iij. jors.	And I saw another surgeon who treated a stone from an old man's bladder, and the stone was large; so he carried off with him a piece of the bladder, and the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called to treat him, and saw the patient's condition and the great size of the stone, and knew well that if it was not removed he would die.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui prist en cure .i. duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi .i. termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And I saw another surgeon who took in charge the leg of a duke from our land, which was broken and had an open wound; and the ignorant surgeon stretched the break over the wound by force, and did not leave the wound any dressing, and left it thus for some time; and commanded that he should not be removed, and so remained until the leg became all inflamed and the foot came to ruin.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to come to him and I hastened to come to loosen the leg; and when I had loosened it, he was at peace and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But in any case the corruption was already confirmed in the member, and I could not heal it; and the corruption did not cease to spread through the member until the member was entirely lost.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I saw another surgeon who opened up an abscess that had become inflamed and then spread through the evil of his authority.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For a chancre, when it is purged of melancholic humor, should not be touched with iron unless one can remove all that which is corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en .ij. divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And therefore, dear son, it is necessary that you know that the work of hands is divided into two divisions: namely, one where there is danger in many dispositions; and I will show in each place of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	Por quoi il est besoig que vous vous en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vous. Si prenez vos armes en cuisson, et entreprenez vos maux légèrement et fermement, et usez de la meilleure voie si que par la grâce de Dieu vous veniez à salut et soiiez loués; et laissez les maux espérables de grande santé; et ostez vos armes de ce que vos fait douter, et ayez foi en vous si que vous puissiez venir de cet monde à l’autre de gloire.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Galens says in some of his admonitions: "Take not care for a bad disease unless you are called foolish doctor.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have divided this treatise into three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapter is about fire cauterization and medical cauterization, and it is the chapter organized from the head to the feet; and about the forms of instruments, and the tools for cauterizing, and all that is necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and about poultices and wounds, and about extracting arrows, and similar things; and it is the chapter organized with forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twistings, and similar things; and it is organized from the head to the feet, with forms of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Therefore that we remember the work, it is necessary that I say the quality of the aid and the harm of each temperament.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the quality of aid and harm is a longer speech and subtle science, and secret answers; and many wise men have spoken about this and agreed with it; and I am short on their words, for I fear the length.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que .ij. complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that cauterization helps universally to all temperaments where there is matter, except for two temperaments: namely, hot temperament with matter and dry temperament with matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In hot and dry temperament with matter, some divided and said that cauterization is great help; while others said the opposite: that cauterization is of no use in diseases that come from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is hot, and should not be cured with heat or dryness; and says he who said the opposite that cauterization does great help in hot and dry diseases that come into the bodies of men.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you understand the body of man and its moisture according to the temperament of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this saying.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it to be true on many occasions through experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And in any case, do not meddle with it except he who has experienced it and knows through long usage the chapter on cauterization, and the diversity of human temperaments, and their dispositions and causes of diseases, and the remedies and expectations of the time; we have no fear for other complexions, especially in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the doctors assembled and agreed on cauterization.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, son, that cauterization with fire is part of the secrets of cures, and of greater virtue than cauterization by burning medicines.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and does not go beyond the member that is burned, and does not harm another member unless it is named.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	The burning medicines come from member to member by flowing, and bring to the sick member great harm; and by chance kill the patient. The fire, because of its highness and the goodness of its substance, does not do this unless there is an excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And I have found this by experiment and the long experience and study that I have put into the art, and it was based on the truth of things; and because of this, I excuse myself for the length of my speech, for it does not please me to take away from you the secret which is revealed in fire, and the quality of the work, how it repels diseases of the body, as philosophers say in demonstrating; so receive it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they agreed on when the cauterizations should be done and chose precedents.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that cauterization is suitable in all cases, because the ensuing harm is removed by the aid of cauterization; and similarly, if the cauterizations are for necessary and pressing pains that cannot wait for a greater evil to come to the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And never think it, dear son, as foolish doctors do; for the disease that is healed by cauterization has no return; and they say so; but it's not so as they think, because cauterizations are not just medicine that changes complexion, and dries out the humors that are the cause of pain, and surpasses medicine in its speed and value, and for the virtue of its work and authority.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And it is possible that the disease comes to some extent according to the complexion of the patient and the place where the disease is located and its virtue; and excesses are gathered in him through the acquisition of food and similar things, unless it is cauterization administered at the right time or place where there is excess moisture, as with cauterizations for denseness causing pain, and similar things, and such pain does not return; but this happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand why cauterizations are called the last resort of medicine, and this is true; but they do not believe that cauterizations are worth anything after medicine, but their intention is false, and it is cauterization that is the last resort of medicine because when we administer methods of treatment for some disease and they do not work, then we administer the cautery, and it is effective.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore it is clear that cauterization is the last resort of medicine, not according to the intention of foolish doctors.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that cauterization with gold is more effective than with iron, and they did not say this unless it was due to the quality of the gold and the purity of its substance; and they said that the place of cauterization does not cause corruption, but this is not true for I have tested it, and I have found that it is true in some men; and gold cauterizations are more effective than iron, as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And yet, when you heat an instrument of gold, you do not know when it is hot by the color of the gold, and it cools down soon; and if you heat it too much, it becomes ruined at the fire; and thus there is enough obstruction.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And therefore we use fire cauterization because we have found it to be suitable for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	And I have ordered this chapter from the beginning to the end, so that the view may be more light for you to find.
dou cautere olivaire	of the olive cauterization
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cauterization is worth against moisture and cold on the head, and there are two ways in which it is done due to the cause of a disease called "soda", and due to many humors that descend from the head to the eyes, and to the ears, and because of excessive dreams and pain in the teeth and throat, and similarly for all diseases that come from cold such as paralysis, apoplexy, and similar diseases.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief .iij. nuis ou .iiij., selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cauterization is that the patient be purged by a dissolving medicine, moistening the head three or four times, according to what the virtue and age and habit of the patient can endure; and then restore the patient's head.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses .ij. eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then make him sit crossed in your hands, and put his hands on the weight; after that, place the root of your palm on the root of his nose between his two eyes; and let your two thumbs come together, so it will bleed a little, then cauterize the "olive" cautery which is this form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os .i. sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren .i. poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse .iij. jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place it on the marked spot with ink, and make it descend and spread your hand little by little in rotating; then lift your hand suddenly, and reward the spot if you see the bone one small step away; and if you don't see it, start the cauterization again until you see the bone as I told you. After that, take a piece of silk, and put it in a soft and moist cotton filling, and place it on the spot, and leave it for three days. Then apply a moistened cloth to butter; and leave it on until the scab is removed. Finally, treat the wound with ointment called "tetrafarmakon" until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And the ancients said that when a wound remains open longer, it purges more thoroughly; and therefore it is more effective.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And some of them said that one should cauterize as much so that part of the bone is burned, and then remove what has been burned from the bone, and treat it.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme .i. vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And the others say that one should cauterize as much above, and push so hard until the bone is worn away as wide as a thimble used by women to let the humors escape; and one should leave the wound open for a long time; after which one should treat and soothe it.
Et ces .ij. manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two methods of cauterization do not seem to me to be entirely good in all respects, except perhaps in some people who have a tendency towards fear; and it seems to me that I should leave it alone; for the head is weakened by the continuous solutions of nature, as we see in other members; and similarly when the patient's head is weak by nature, and the first appearance of cauterization is more salutary and conducive to health for me, and with this principle I work in all cases.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	from ancient pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When chronic pain comes to the head and lasts long, the patient should use year's powder and pills called "cochie", and for purging of the head, oils and emplasters; and if one makes the cautery that we have previously said, it does not help.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take care if the patient's head is of strong nature and not too cold; then apply a cautery below that previous one.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai .i. cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est .i. leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After, apply a cautery on each horn of the head just to the bone, as we have said before, and make one cautery at the place called "vasselz"; and there is one place where you put poultices; and hold your hand so that you don't see just to the bone: the patient feels too much greater pain in this cautery than in others, and I will speak of it later; and it is necessary that the cauterizations on the horns be more subtle than those used for cauterizing the middle part of the head, and that's the form:
dou cautere dou chief	of the head cautery
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc .ij. manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When sudden pain comes to one part of the head and spreads to the eye, and the patient's head is purged by medicinal medicines, and all other cures that I have said in the division of diseases are tried, and none of this does any good: then make cauterizations according to two ways, that is to say, with medicinal water and fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope .i. poc as .ij. chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi .xij. houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi .ij. jors ou .iij.; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The cauterization with medicinal water is such that you take a dose of almonds, remove the skin and crush it into one part as two heads, and then make the temple where the pain holds in this way so that you can place the almond dose under the skin; and when it is placed, bind and tighten it well and leave it thus for 12 hours; then release it and let the almond juice flow away, and leave the wound thus for 2 or 3 days; then put a cloth soaked in butter on it as long as the pus issues.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the ointment cure as long as it is healed; and if you see that this does not help, then make use of some burning medicines that I have written about or in the treatise on burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The iron cautery is done according to this method.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery until it takes its shape.
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait .i. poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And it is called "clos" because the head is made in the shape of a bell or a horn with a small curve, and it has a little bit of a rounded appearance; and one puts it on the painful place, and holds your hand and turns the fire slightly, so that the middle part of the core is burned; and lift your hand lest the artery burn, which is outside, and stop the abundance of blood.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par .iij. jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	After put cotton in oil of silk, and put it on the place for 3 days; then I put moistened cotton in butter, and then cure the place with ointment until it is healed; and if you want to cauterize this migraine with the cautery called "cultellare", at all points, and take care not to cut off the artery in this migraine which is not an old one.
de emigraine	of migraine
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you cure migraine as we have said before in the divisions of diseases, and it does not help, and you see that the cauterizations previously described from medicine and fire do not benefit, then it is necessary that you heat the cautery called "cultellare" until it is white; and afterwards place it on the painful place a line half a digit long, and take your hand once, and strain so that you do not cut off the artery and come just to the bone; and beware of the jaw that moves when eating, and the nerve has regard only for the movement and spasm does not come to the patient, and beware of the cessation of blood from the artery when it is cut, or the cutting be great fear and especially for one who does not know, and who is not a student or experienced; and leave the work in my way; but I will tell you how to stop blood when the artery is cut, and I will show you where it applies in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait .ij. coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you see that these cauterizations do not benefit the disease, and the patient is suffering, then cauterize the enemy in the head as we have said, and cure the wound until it is healed; and if you see fit, administer the cautery that we have said in the chapter on extraction of the artery, with the cautery that has two knives; and this cautery is better than the other and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	of ear pain from coldness
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When ear pain comes from coldness and one has tried medicines that dissolve and other cures that we have said in the division, and the pains do not subside, then heat this cautery which is called "poins", according to the form:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les .ij. se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait .x. poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After, puncture all around the sick ear, or around both if the pain is in both, and remove a little above the root of the ear after you have marked the place to puncture; and make 10 punctures around each ear; then cure the wound until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	of mouth torture
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	Torture that must be cured by cauterization is not except those that move from phlegm, as we have said in the divisions of diseases; and do not make a cauterization on similar things that come from scorching and spasms of nerves.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de .iij. cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des .ij. levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you cure this semblance of torture that moves from phlegm and from purging of the head and gargling, and it does not work, then it is necessary to cauterize the patient with three cauterizations: one in the root of the ear, and another a little outside the temple, and the third in the joint of the two lips; and place the cautery on the part that appears healthy, and make the cautery near the head of the ear above a small piece of bone, and another on the temple as long as a pea; and leave the cautery until the middle part of the core is burned; and this is the form of the cauterization:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And this is similar to the "cultellare" that we have mentioned before, but it is a little more subtle and requires that the knife be a little thicker; afterwards, cure the wound as I have said before, until it is healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai .iiij. cauteres: .ij. sus les .ij. cornes dou chief, et .i. emmi le chief, et .i. ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexy is old and you cure it as we have said, and it does not help, and the patient has no fever, then make three cauterizations: two on the two horns of the head, and one in the middle of the head, and one at the place called "vasselz" as we have said before, and the last cauterization is on the mouth of the stomach; and be cured as we have said before.
de litargie	From lethargy
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	To this disease it is good to give the patient great pills and powder-like things for the brain; afterwards, he should rub the chief of the patient all over, and put on top of the back of the head a poultice of mustard as written in the treatise on poultices; and this is the manner of cauterization: if he does it just as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai .iij. cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere .i. doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai .i. cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, .ij. autres sus les .ij. cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If he is healed thus, it is good; and if not, then make three cauterizations around the head, descending just to the neck, and leave a space of one or two fingerbreadths between each cauterization; and cure him as with the others, and if you see any swelling or inflammation, make one cauterization in the middle; and if necessary, two more on the two horns, and cure until he is healed; and that cauterization which is called "olivare", just as I have said before.
de la froidor dou chief	from chill of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et .i. derrier et .iij. sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai .iiij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	It is necessary that the head be purged with years and what we have said before; afterwards, rub the patient's head, then make a cauterization in the head and on each horn, and one behind and three on the spine of the neck; and if you need more, and the body is moist and the patient is suffering, and the disease is spreading, make four cauterizations on the spine of the back; and let it be until the most of the burn is done, and lift your hand; afterwards, cure him until he is healed, and that cauterization which is called "olivare" as we have said before.
de l’epilempsie	of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	Epileptics should not use cauterization unless they are phlegmatic, and it is necessary first to purge the brain with years and other cures that we have said in the division when the patient is large and suffering from poor medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai .i. cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et .i. cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if it is an infant who cannot suffer it, make him gargarism and mastication to purge the brain often with good meats; afterwards, rub the head in the middle, and make one cauterization as we have said before, and one on the base of the skull, and on each horn; and if the patient is spreading and suffering, make cauterizations just as I have said for someone who has paralysis and softening of the body, on the spine of the back and neck, and let it be the "olivier" cauterization according to the manner that I have said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai .i. cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is an infant, make one subtle cauterization in this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When by the cause of melancholy the superfluities or moistures are corrupted and thick phlegm is formed, then make those cauterizations as we have said for someone who has paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if by the cause of melancholy the superfluities are declining into melancholy, and the patient's body is moist, then give him something to drink that will purge the brain, according to what is said before in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai .i. torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com .i. cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After rubbing the patient's head, after make one bandage of well-made linen, like a circle, and put it on top of the head; and the patient should be crossed, and held tightly from all sides; afterwards, apply the ointment, and anoint with butter of ancient herbs; and heat it over temperate fire, so that the patient can bear to have it poured on them; after, empty the circle inside the head, and let it cool; and do this for the patient once a week for good governance, until they are healed.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	Or if you see that it is being cauterized by making several points all over the cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	This method of cauterization moistens the brain sufficiently; and then put on a wet cloth in butter and hen fat.
de l’awe des eulz	of the eyes' evil
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When evil comes first to the eyes by the signs that I said in the division, then begin and give the patient something to drink that purifies the head, and watch out for all moisture, and make him sweat or take a bath several times while fasting.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as .ij. eulz ensamble, ou en .i. se li dessendemens est en .i.; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	After that, command the patient to rub their head backwards, and make a cauterization in the head, and make two cauterizations on each temple if the evil descends from one eye to the other together, or if it descends from one to one; and seal all the veins and arteries that are under the scalp, and let the cauterization be long according to the width of the temple; and watch out for hemorrhage of blood, and if you see too much blood coming out, then stop as best you can.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les .ij. os derrier.	And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and at incision how to stop the bleeding; and never make a cauterization or incision under the two bones behind.
dou cors des larmes	of the tears of the heart
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: .i. cautere emmi le chief, et .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples, et .ij. cauteres ou haiterel desoz les .ij. os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout .i. petit cautere.	When the tears of the eyes are old and accustomed and are above the veins or below the arteries that appear on the forehead; and one sees that it is cold, phlegmatic superfluity, then make the cauterization that I said at the beginning of the evil descending to the eyes: one cauterization in the head, two cauterizations on each temple, and two cauterizations or incisions under the two bones; and if there is need for more, then cauterize carefully above the eyebrow for every small cauterization.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	of the tears of the heart within the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide .iij. nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai .ij. cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les .ij. sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you medicate according to what we have said in the division, and it does not help, then give the patient three cooked figs to drink; afterwards, rub the head, and make a cauterization in the middle of the "olivary" cauterization; and make two cauterizations of the "clavilis" cauterization on each eyebrow, a little below the hairline; and watch out for the artery so that you do not cover it.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the cauterization called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the parchment of oil is softened by disease and moisture, then cauterize it with this caustic called "olivare".
de coi ci est li forme:	Until it takes its shape.
Et se tu vues si fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you see that it makes two cauterizations on each eyebrow, as long as the eyebrow is; and do not leave your hand there except until one-third of the paper is burned, according to the manner that I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	of the hair that points the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	Never has it happened that the eyelashes are converted to the inside and point at the eye, and make cauterizations in two ways: namely, by fire or by burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	Or cauterization by fire: command the patient to leave the eyelashes as long and equal as they are; and if they point at their birth, then bind his eyes so that they do not move until they have been born.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they are born and are equal, then place the patient in a warm bath; afterwards mark on the paper with eyes an image that is like the leaf of myrtle, and note the beginning of the sign below the hairs; then apply moist cotton to the eye in egg white and persimmon juice, then warm the cautery whose form is this:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi .iij. jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After cauterizing on the figure that you have marked bit by bit many times, so that the burns are spread out around; and the signs of the health of the work are when you see the paper retracted, and the hairs raised to the level of the eye; then lift your hand, and let it be like this for three days, then apply moist cotton in butter until the blister is removed; afterwards anoint with ointment until they are healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if after this the hairs come, and the paper is softened then start again with the cautery on the same place, as you did first; and if the hairs are gone, then cauterize until the paper is raised to its natural level and is even, and do not prick the hairs into the eye.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en .i. oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en .i., et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse .i. poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The burning cautery of medicine is that you instruct the patient to let their hairs grow long and even; then make a parchment form of the leaf of myrtle; then take French soap and live coal, each one third, and mix them together well; and do this quickly, so it does not cool down, then place it on the form that you have made like the leaf of myrtle, and put it on the paper with eyes; and if the disease stays in one eye only, then work on one, and if in both alike; and apply moist cotton under the eye in egg white; and the patient's head is in a warm bath and place your two fingers showing on the medicine, and press a little bit at a time every time the patient feels the stinging of the medicine, because they feel it like fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, then take away the medicine from your hand.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	And when the ulceration has passed, then lift the lid of the abscess, and look if you see the parchment lifted as if it had been lifted by constraint of fire or incision; and if so, it is well.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If not, then apply more medicine to the abscess or let it have no effect, until your works are equal, and your eyes are set in order; then put on a wet cloth in butter until the burns are gone, after curing the abscess of ointment which is called "dyafenis" and others, until it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if it is necessary for you to take great care with your work so that it does not fail in the eyes of others.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if the paper becomes soft afterwards, and the hair pricks in the eye, then begin the medicine again on that same spot which has been softened by the paper properly, just as you did before; apply it so long as it is healing; and this is the form of the mirabilis leaf.
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that the eyes of men are diverse in size and smallness, and according to these you must make your constrains; and do not assume the right path for one who has no study of this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	(Note: This appears to be a new section header, indicating that the text is about to describe a different medical procedure or treatment.)
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you cure a fistula as we have said in the divisions of diseases, and your cures do not help, then it is necessary that you make it cauterized according to this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to put their head in your warm bath; and hold the patient's head between your hands in such a way that it does not move, nor will they take their head away; afterwards apply moist cotton in egg white or persimmon juice to the eye; afterwards warm the cautery which is this: and shape it into a curved form like a vulture's beak, together with the cautery; if you see, then mark from one end of the head to the other, and if you see, then make it like a tent; but all the same, what is shaped will move for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	Afterwards compress the fistula if it is open, and remove any purulence and dryness; and if it is closed, then open it up and pull out the plug; afterwards apply the hot cautery strongly, and hold your hand on the cautery at the part of the eye above the pupil, so that your hands do not become foolish; and put the cautery into the fatty part of the eye and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the beginning of the cautery just up to the bone, it would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If not, then start the cautery again once more, and if necessary, and leave it for three days; afterwards put on a moist cotton poultice in butter, and apply the drying ointment so long as it is healing, and if forty days pass and it is not healed, then put on corrosive medicine until the bone is exposed; and let it rest according to what comes in its chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a way of doing a cautery on a fistula that none of the ancients said.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	You understand a fistula, and open the place; afterwards put in the subtle canal which is the shape:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	and make it to the quantity of one third of a lump; and hold your hand or camel hair firmly, and do not let the patient move until the lump melts into their eye; and it is necessary that you apply moist cotton in egg whites or in awe: the lump thus cures the fistula, and brings about marvelous health.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed through the cautery that we have said, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If not, then it is necessary to make a perforation in the navel, and bring the fistula back to its natural place within the navel according to what is fitting for its own location.
des crevaices en levres	(Note: This appears to be a new section header, indicating that the text is about to describe a different medical procedure or treatment.)
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times there occur cracks in lips called "fissures", and similarly in children's lips.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe .i. petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these cracks as we have said in the divisions, and the treatment does not help, then warm a small surgical cauterizer according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And apply it quickly into those cracks until it becomes full; afterwards cure the skin with cerote until it is healed.
de l’aposteme de la goule	(Note: This appears to be a new section header, indicating that the text is about to describe a different medical procedure or treatment.)
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies .i. cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou .ij., aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When aposteme comes to the root of the throat or in the uvula or palate, or at the roots of the teeth; and it festers and rots and becomes a fistula; and you treat it as we have said in divisions, and it does not help: then it is necessary that you make a cauterization according to the size of the fistula; afterwards plug or stop the fistula, and hold your hand until the iron becomes hot at the fontanelle and behind the ear; and do so once or twice, after the treatment as we have said in cures, until it is healed; and if it is cured thus, it's good; and if not, then it is necessary to uncover the skin and remove the corrupted bone, according to what you will find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	of movement of teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicines but it doesn't work, then put the patient's head in your hand; afterwards sharpen the cautery so that the form will come after in this manner as if you were putting a cord on a tooth; and put hot hastily inside the cautery and hold your hand until the patient feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth; afterwards lift up your hand and restart the cautery according to your pleasure; afterwards fill the patient's mouth with salted water, and let it stay an hour and rich fever.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this manner the teeth that were moving are fixed, and the gums softened are restrained, and the moisture corrupted is dried.
de la dolor des dens	of the pain of the teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc .ij. manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When the pain of teeth comes from coldness, whether there is cold or heat, and medicines do not work, then it is necessary to cauterize in two ways: cauterizing with butter and cauterizing by fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus .i. fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Cauterizing with butter is such that you take butter from a cow, and the end of it in an iron or clay spoon; afterwards take cotton and wrap it around the point of a tent, and soak it in hot butter, and put it on the painful tooth quickly and hold until it cools down; and thus do often until its virtue comes to the root of the tooth, and if you see that wool and cotton are soaked in cold butter, and put it on the painful tooth, and put a hot iron on top until the fire comes to the crown of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	The cautery is accompanied by fire such that you take a piece of iron or bronze, and it should be thick so that the flame does not reach the mouth of the patient; afterwards heat the cautery, thus the shape will come after, and put it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery is cooled; do this often, for the pain will be removed that very day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it is necessary that the patient fill his mouth with good butter in the pressure of this cautery, and then let it flow forth; and this is the form of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And do the cautery however you want, and according to what you can do; and this is the form of the cord:
des scrophules	of scrofulas
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the scrofulae are of mucus and cold moisture, and do not obey digestion by medicines, then heat the cautery so that it comes to the form, and has two openings for the fumes to issue from the other part; and place the hot cautery on the abscess once, or as needed, until it reaches the center of the abscess; and if the abscess is small, place a cautery according to its size, and leave it thus three days; and apply a moist cloth soaked in butter until the inflammation is removed; afterwards treat with ointments and tents until it is healed.
Li forme de la cainne:	The form of the gut:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When the moistures prevail on the channels of the womb, and especially when it comes from cold complexion, then it is necessary that the patient be purged first by soluble medicines; afterwards make a fire cautery at the root of the throat, and take care not to come all the way to the throat, but only up to a little bit.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	Afterwards make another cautery at the joint of the neck at the top of the spine, and it is called "clavicle" for which we have the form before; and take care of the place as we said before until it is healed.
de la toust	of the throat
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et .i. autre cautere emmi le pis entre .ij. mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When all and every disease of the peritoneum are of cold moisture, and the patient has no fever or heat, and is an old illness, then make two cauterizers on the navel in the usual place; and one other cauterizer inside the chest between the breasts; and this is the cauterizer called "clavicle" according to the form which is said before.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	And if you see, make a cautery in piercing all the cautery that is called "points" for which the form is here before in the disease of the ears; and be the points up to thirty or around.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	After healing according to what is said above, and having the fire cauterization at three rings according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais .iij. a cop.	And therefore are the cauterers lighter, because you make them in triplicate.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	(unchanged translation from earlier)
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a .ij. ners douqueil ci est li forme:	Afterwards be careful of the patient on their back and on their side; afterwards lift up the skin which is inside the titillate with your left hand; and if the jointure is dislocated inside, then sharpen the cauterizer which has two horns as described before:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble .iiij. cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a .iij. ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a .iij. ners:	and cauterize the skin until it is pierced all the way to the side, and the figure of the cauterization will come with three cauterizers; and for this reason is made the cauterizer with the cauterizer which has three horns, because the figure of cauterization are six cauterizers; and are the nerves according to the subtlety of a tent, and this is the form of the cauterizer which has three horns:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce .i. nerf por coi il i a .viij. cauteres.	And once is added to that one nerve for which there are eight cauterizers.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	Afterwards put on the cauterizer powder mixed with silk; afterwards make the patient rest, and do not move their limbs for a long time until they are well comforted.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated above, little good happens then, so make a cauterization on the thick part of the cauterized skull, or many cauterizations in pricking.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joint is closed, and moisture is removed, and the patient is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When coldness and much moisture come to the stomach, and they trouble his complexion, and there are many cathartics for him, and he is accustomed to the usual cures but does not benefit, then it is necessary that the patient lies down on his back, stretches out his legs and arms.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	Then I make three cauterizations one under the breastbone of a hen's size, all along the cauterized skull, and two cauterizations on both sides so that the shape of the cauterizations is at three angles, and there be such space between one and another that they are not joined together when they will give harm; and the cauterization should be so deep that it reaches the two parts of the skin, and the shape of the cauterizations should be according to this form without addition.
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if you see someone being cauterized with a great fire brand in the stomach according to this form; and he who has fear of this cauterization, cauterize suddenly and mark on the stomach i. point according to the quantity that you see of incision; then cauterize all the way to the point which is called "poins".
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the care of the wound that we had before, until he be healed.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	When the liver comes into pain from cold and moisture and great windiness, as long as it is excessively disturbed from its natural complexion by superfluities; and the patient is treated according to what we have said in divisions, and it does not help him, then the patient must be counseled to take his breath deeply; and mark three cauterizations according to this form and figure and quantity on the liver, below the ribs, where the flank of man comes; and leave a space between each cauterization the thickness of a finger; and let the cauterization be as long as the length of the body, and do not press too hard with your hand all along the cauterization; and burn only the middle of the incision, and have the patient sit upright on his feet; and if he cannot, then support him, stretch out his legs, and lift up his arms.
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	Et if your will is, then cauterize these cauteries with the cutlery, if you are subtle and skilled in the art, and beware that you do not burn all the way through the key, for you would dry out the entire body; and it should not come just to boiling, for the keys are very subtle there at the point, and you know this truly.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	When he has an abscess on the liver, and you want to know if it is in the flesh of the liver or in the membrane: if it is in the flesh, then the patient feels pain not too strong; and if it is in the membrane, then the patient feels unbearable pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	And then when the cure is over the mirrors, it is necessary that the patient be placed on their back above their head; and then mark with an iron point where the abscess is, and then heat the cautery which is similar to a raisin, from which comes the shape:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, and viegne jusc'a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu'il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l'art de medicine, and par cui mains ces maladies ont corrut aucune fois.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	He can work boldly, and it seems to me that it is better to leave them.
dou cautere de pleuresin	of the cauterizing for pleurisy
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize .i. cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et .ij. petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et .ij. cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et .i. cautere emmi le pis, et .i. autre sus l’estomac, et .i. entre .ij. espaules, et .ij. as .ij. costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre .ij. espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancients said that one should make cauterizers for pleurisy using roots of Aristolochia, and in this manner: take a long root of Aristolochia, the largest you can find, and let it be dry, and as thick and as long as your arm; soak it in oil, and put it on the fire, and cauterize one cauterizer between the navel and the neck, and two small cauterizers a little lower down in the part that is below the beard; and two cauterizers between the fifth rib and the sixth, declining a little; and one cauterizer inside the chest, and one other on the stomach, and one between the shoulders, and two on the ribs outside the cauterizer that is between the shoulders; and do not press your hand, but make it appear openly just as in smelling.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	And they say that some old men advise to use a fire cauterization similar to shaving, and heat it up and put it between the ribs, until it reaches the abscess; and then the pain subsides, as we have said in the abscess of the liver.
