Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this work there is fear for the patient who dies now, or a fistula comes that cannot be healed.
de la mice	Of the mouse
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent .iij. manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you cure the disease of the mouse according to what we have said about the divisions of cures, and it does not benefit, then there are three ways of cauterization that are all good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	Of which one manner is that you make three cauterizations, or four, in a line according to the length of the abscess, according to the figure of the liver cauterization that we have said before; and do not press your hand on all the cauterization, and let the patient be aware on his back; and another manner of cauterization is that you heat up the cauterization which has two horns, as we have shown in the dislocation of the shoulder; and lift the key which is near the abscess, or the ribs of the patient come towards the left side, and let the elevations be according to the key, according to the length of the body, and the cauterization be according to the width of the body.
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	After I put the two needles inflamed until the kidneys are perceived from the other side, and then treat with fire the cautery, and thus there will be four; if you see, then cauterize the entire cautery to three needles.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the cure when he has got a purpuration by long time, and this is like the others of the cures said before.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	The cautery is not good for dropsy, unless it is done in the manner called "asclytes".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	When you cure him according to the manners that we have said in divisions, and your cure does not benefit, then it is necessary that you give him four cauterizations around the mouth, and one on the stomach, and one on the liver, and one on the spleen, and two behind the back on the spine, and one in front of the breast; and let the cauterizations be well near the seat of the kidney.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les .ij. ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	Then leave the cauterization open to get rid of inflammation for a long time, and do not cease the cure of the patient after the cauterization; and recovery will hasten, and the two intentions will be together with the help of God.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The form of the cauterizer for the belly is the key that we have shown before; and that one for the back is olive-like, according to what was said before.
de l’enfleure des piez	of the swelling of the pines
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	When the feet are swollen in someone who is dropsy-prone and are full of yellow water, it is necessary that you cauterize on the back of the foot between the little finger and the ring finger; and lift your hand with the cautery so as to turn.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not enter too far in, thus the yellow water would burst forth, and the cauterize should be according to this form:
Aprés fai sus .ij. jambes .ij. cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	Then make two cauterizations on each leg at the tip of the calcanean bone; and let the cauterization be long, one under the knee in front and the other behind, within the leg; and leave the cauterization open for a long time without curing, until the yellowish moisture is gone; after that, cure the patient with the other cures that we have said.
de la menoison	of menstruation
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai .i. grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et .iiij. cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout .i. cautere clavile subtil, et .ij. cauteres sus les hainches.	When the flux of the womb comes from cold and moisture, so that the retaining and digestive virtues which are in the stomach and intestines are weakened, and cannot be cured by any methods; and you see the patient suffering greatly and with great virtue, then make one large cauterization on the stomach according to what has been said before about the stomach cauterization at the cauterization of the belly, and three fine cauterizations around the mouth as delicate as each key is subtle, and two cauterizations on the hips.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et .i. cautere sus chaicun yle, et .ij. petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see the moisture abounding and the patient suffering, then make one cauterization on the navel, and one cauterization on each rib, and two small cauterizations on the stomach below the large one, because the cure is beneficial when there is good aid.
de la cure des emorroydes	of the cure of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	When the hemorrhoids are in the fundament, one or more, and are ancient and are made of thick, cold, moist corrupted humors, and are treated as we have said in divisions, and it does not help, then make cauterizations: three on the spine of the back, that which is entirely below the almond-shaped mole and increasing triangularly, and one cauterization under the jaw, two on the abdomen; and if you think that their stomach is chilled, and the food does not cook, and the face swells up, then make a large cauterization on the stomach, as it was said before, and another on the liver, and another on the spleen to all the cautery nails; and leave the cautery open for a long time.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After treatment let it rest until it is healed.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the swelling which is called "Thelul"
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you cope with Thelul, then heat the cauterizer which seems like a razor, and then set it on fire all around that Thelul to be coped; and I leave my hand there as long as the cauterization comes to the edge of the vein, so that the blood does not flow; do this once or twice, and if there is much Thelul, then cauterize each one as we have said; after that, cure with ointments which are beneficial until they are sound; and if you cauterize with a great cauterizer on Alchatim, it will have greater aid.
de plaie mal curee	of an ill-cured wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot bear cutting or opening, as we will tell in its place, then comes this disease which cannot be healed except by cauterization.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When someone has a fistula, and it is inflamed and discharges foul-smelling pus and corrupted moisture, then you must carefully examine the entire tent (fold) to its deepest part.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	After cauterizing the area that appears to be razor-sharp, and plugging it into the fistula according to the amount that the tent has entered, and recommence cauterizing until the corrupted flesh is burned away, once or twice or three times, depending on the amount of harm; and beware of burning the nerves that are nearby, and the large veins.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	If the fistula goes into the bladder and intestine, then beware of these parts, and do not make fires except in burned flesh, and think that it is not perishing; after treatment let it rest until it is healed, and if the parts are sore, and the matters are removed over a long time, then know that the parts are entirely healed; and if the matters are not removed, know that the parts are torn, and corrupted bone to the front; and thus as one of those that we will say in its place.
de la maladie des reins	From the disease of the kidneys
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When the pain of cold comes to the kidneys, and great windiness, and does not take on a woman's shape, then it is necessary that you make a cautery on the kidneys on one side and the other at the cauterizing nail that we have previously said; and if we were to cauterize in mid-air, there would be .iii. cauterizations in line, and they will do more great help.
de la vessie	Of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is soft and weak from cold and moisture, so that the patient retains urine, then make a cautery on the part behind the bladder, where the hairs of the urethral opening begin, and one on the right and one on the left, and each should be as long as a thumb's breadth; and make one cauterization behind the back, or two if you need them; and let the cauterizations be nail-like according to the form previously said.
de la marris	Of the womb
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the womb is cold and moist, and does not allow conception for that reason, and the flowers are corrupted and their terms are late; and when they come, there is great pain: then it is necessary to make three cauterizations around the mouth, as we have said in the cautery of the bladder, and two cauterizations behind the back; and let the cauterizations be nail-like, as we have said.
de la hainche	Of the intestines
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the viscous moistures descend to the cecum of the intestines, and because of this they move out of their place, and the sign is that the hip is longer than the other when measured together; and it is found that the swelling of the departure vein is there, then it is necessary that you cauterize the patient on the cecum of the intestines at one cauterization like a circle, and sign before the swelling around the cecum as it turns, so that the cecum is inside the circle; and let the cauterizations be such as those by which we have cauterized the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if these cauterizations are not present, then make three great cauterizations of the olive-like shape, and let the cauterizations be as deep as all the keys; and heal until it is sound.
de la dolor de la hainche	Of the pain in the intestines
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes to the cecum of the intestines, and it is from cold and moisture, and the patient is cured by what we have said in the division, but the cure does not prevail, and the disease is old: then it is necessary that you purge the patient of thick humors with fetid pills or other good-looking pills similar to these.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	After the fire cautery; and the manner of the cautery is according to two manners: that is to say, together with burning medicines, and fire cautery.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	Fire cautery is according to many manners, one of which is: that you cauterize on the back of the thigh three triangular cauterizations in this form, and make good depth and great, and have between each cauterization the width of a thumb, and be the cauterizations olive-shaped; sometimes a cauterization is made in the middle on the head of the thigh, so that there are four according to this form:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see, then cauterize at the cauterization of the circle that we have said before in the dislocation of the intestines; but make it in this way so that the circles contain all the intestines, and all the keys of the keur are burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And it is the manner in which one does it in sciatica, when the pain holds in the thigh and does not reach as far as the hip or as far as the leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if it comes as far as the hip and leg, make two cauterizations on the side where the patient says the pain is, and one cauterization above the ankle four fingers thick, a little to the left; and let the cauterizations be cleft-shaped, and let the thickness of the key be burnt; and if the patient feels that the pain extends as far as two inches or nearly so from the foot, then cauterize where they feel the pain three points or four at the cautery called "points".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if it is necessary to do more; and if he knows that the pain is below the kneecap towards the hip, then make a cauterization at the cutellate or circular cauterization, and take good care in all your cauterizations that you do not leave the cautery so long that you burn the nerves and great arteries, and that you do not cause more great nuisance and contraction to the patient.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I myself have seen many who have had a fire cautery on the ankle of the foot, and let them be until the leg was entirely swollen, and the feet also, and were pierced and corrupted all the feet.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After a purgation of the belly from which he died.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pains are in two parts together, make a fire cautery on one and on the other, according to this manner.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And the wise men say in the cauterization of the flank, this is how it should be done, make such a fire and let it be as big as a walnut or a little less, and let it be between the ribs and let it be so that there is a gap of the quantity of a bean's width; and let the intervals be two fingers wide, and also like beans, and one inch of iron well made; and this is the form:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Here is the translation:
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we should use this cautery not from fear of its gaze, and if few people are seen who use it; yet this is one of the good cauteries which can be endured, and there where it applies.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	The cauteries of burning medicine are such that you make an instrument to be interchanged in which the edges of the door descend, and it is made of earth or iron with a length of one part, and on the top have two notches, and between each notch have the quantity of the size of a dove; and they should be open above and below, and come together as a whole according to this form:
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	After put the bony ridge of the back on the patient lying on a warm stone, and then place your hand above the bony ridge; after that pour hot water between the two circles of the pot which has been heated over fire one part, and let it stay for an hour or a time, and allow the patient to feel the heat and burning.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is also true that there is inflammation like fire; and when the inflammation has passed, lift your hand with the instrument and lift the hot water off the patient, and let it be so for three days, and apply butter until what is black from scabbing is removed; and after three days of purging, this would be the final aid after the cure of ointments as long as they are healed.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	And if the pain has spread to the hip or the knee, then make the instrument that takes hold according to what you have done in the right way; and this is the method of hot water, and I have written it or treated it in the book of correction of medicine.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take alkali and hot water, as much of one as the other, and grind them together, and put them in a new pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	where there is a small hole to pour out what the tip of a razor can enter; and put it into another pot well weighted, and put hot water on top of alkali and sweet water above, so that there will be two layers of powder under you'll have well prepared in your hand; and let it sit like this until the liquid at the bottom of the pot becomes clear and free-flowing, then take all that liquid and pour it on hot water and alkali as before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	And then it will be very busy and entrusted to the movement of medical works and other members' cauterizations. For it makes a useful work like fires, and if there are other medicines that one cauterizes well, such as henna, honeyed anacardi, and chalz with soap, all these things mixed together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Galen tells us of a treatment by which one man was cured of the pain in his haunch and sciatic vein, and he greatly praised it, saying that no other treatment was done, and that he became well only once when this treatment was made, and he bathed himself just as he teaches below.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	And he says in the same manner that you take green and dry litharge, and grind it well with a little fat, and apply it to the haunch, hip, and leg where the pain is, and bind; and leave it there for three hours or until the patient no longer feels the burning.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then make him enter the bath until his body is slightly warmed up, and then make him enter the bed, and the pain will go away entirely and he will be healed.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And know that no one should use fire cautery on such medicines unless it is after the evacuation of the body.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And Dioscorides says that when the vein of Sciatic is cauterized with goat's hair fires, it helps a lot; and it should be done in this way.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take linen and soak it in old oil, and place it on the hollow between the thumb of the foot and the other which is called a fleshy fold.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	After that take goat's hair fibers, and soak them in fire until they are charcoal-like, and place them on the linen, and let it sit until it cools; and do it again like this, and do not stop doing it like this until you think by reason that it will come to the hank, and that the pain is ceased; and this method of cautery is called "goat's hair cautery".
de la dolor dou dos	from the pain of the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether from falling or percussion or from too great evacuation, or from similar cold matter spread out, none of these likenesses is worth a cautery except for that which comes from the infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary afterwards that the patient be relieved of fetid pills or similar things, and then one makes three lines marked on the back, where the pain lies, with 5 cauteries or more according to the virtue and quantity that the patient can endure; and let the cautery be made according to the "poins" cautery; and if you see fit, make 3 or 4 cauteres at the cauterized middle point in this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	Many times this disease comes to young children, and the signs of its beginning are that they have a narrow, tight feeling when they wake up, and fear; and you find it in the lower back and also on the appearance that comes over other vertebrae.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you wish to cure it, then cauterize at the "celcle" cautery according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	So the limb must be equally red throughout the cauterization.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see, then cauterize around the spine with a fire cautery two or three lines away from each other, and have the points close to one another.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After the cure, keep the wound so long as it is healing according to what we have said, and beware that you do not apply cauterization in a hollow spot which is near a nerve.
de la dolor des jointes	from the pain of joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When pain of joints is from moisture that is spread out to each member of the body, and when pain comes in feet, which doctors properly call "podagre", and when it is caused by cold matter and medicines cannot cure it, then it is cured by cauteries in this manner: make a large number of cauteres around the joint of the foot, and let the cautery be olive-like according to this form.
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if there is need, then prick on the surface of the foot, so that the fire cautery claims "point".
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if the pains come just to the knee and other joints, and this happens many times, then make a fire cautery on each kneecap three or four times, to the entire olive-shaped area; and if you need more, do more, but do not hold your hand there longer than until the skin of the key is burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend as far as the knee and back, administer the fire cautery that we have said in its chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are in the hands, make pinpricks around the wrist II lines; and if there remains no pain to the elbow, make pinpricks above each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come as far as the shoulders or as far as the armpits, cauterize each part, and make good governance over the patient and administer medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you make good governance and purge phlegm, he will be healed with the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	of the roughness of the scurf.
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When itch comes to the angles, and the boils descend to the groin and it is new, then it is necessary that when you see it cured, it does not get worse that day; and that it uses things that make the belly loose, so that the phlegm descends from its stomach; after which have it sit on his back between your hands, and command him to hold his breath until the boils are healed, and then bring them to your feet, and sign with a line below the itch on the bone of the pointing, and make all one sign like half a circle above the body; then shape the cautery according to this form:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	as long as he is white and gives signs.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then reset the bowels to their place; and the attendants hold his hand so that he does not return backward; and work well on the patient's hips, and put a cushion and a servant under him on the hips, and another one on the chest who holds his hands; then put the cautery on the sign on all your hands, and hold it straight and hold it until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it at first, start again as many times as it takes to reach the bone; and be watchful subtly so that the bowel does not burst when you do the cautery; lest you burn him; and that by this the patient may not die or suffer other evils.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that when you do not come close to the bone with the cautery, your work is worth nothing.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And it is necessary that the cauteries of children be subtle according to their size, and those of great people also great according to theirs; after three days, cure the area with butter until the swelling is removed; afterwards, cure other ointments until they are healed, and let the patient lie on his back for 40 days so that the wound is well closed; and it is necessary that their bandages be worn long enough, so that the flesh does not protrude when he will need to go into chambers.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after 40 days, when he wants to get up, give him a well-made bandage and have him wear it for another 40 days; and let him have good rest, so that he does not work too much and watch out for excessive drinking and eating, and high-pitched shouting; and when he follows this instruction, he is fully healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will say next about the treatment of cutting in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	from the itch of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When ulcers come in other bodies and are known, and you see that they do not grow more, then make the fire cautery on the fire according to its quantity, and let the third part of the cure be burned; after the cure according to what we have said; and some of the ancients have said that one should cauterize at the cautery at three angles according to this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but mark the first sign at the beginning and make a line on the width above the ulcer, and another below it, and draw your hand through all the cautery with a nail.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauterizations are lighter and moody.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	from old pain in any member
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes to any member, whether from falling or striking, and that pain lasts for a long time, and the cure of medicine is not worth it, then it is necessary that he be cauterized at the cautery which is called "poins", and the cauteries should be according to the length of the member, its smallness, weakness, and virtue, and its location of torments and pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If he is healed from the first cautery, it is well; if not, begin another cautery on that one, for those customs are that it should be moved to the member which is closest, therefore you must make cauterizations until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	of surgery
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The humors are helped sometimes by cautery with great help, and similarly the disease that comes from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	Can you not see it being cauterized, take care if the disease is at its beginning, and if it has been cured according to what we have said in the division, and does not spread nor remain, and you doubt that corruption will overpower the whole patient, then make five cauterizations on the head: one on top of the head, and the other towards the forehead to the end of the eyebrows; and two on each horn, and one behind on the occipital bone; and leave your hand there until the cautery reaches the bone, and until the scales come out so that the vapors of the gross humors can come out; and cauterize on the mouse according to what is before.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the surgery is spread everywhere; and it is manifestly declining, then it is necessary that you cauterize with these cauteries on the head, and one on the navel, and two on each spine of the neck, and six on each spine of the back, and one large one on the scullion and another below, and two on each shoulder; and two on each flank, and two on each tendon of the breast, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and take heed of the nerves that are beneath the last calcination, lest you burn them; and sometimes make a cautery on the bone of the wrist, and another on the bone of the stomach, and another on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And know that the more I make of a cautery, the more it helps him, and brings greater benefit; and know that the patient does not feel pain at the cautery as healthy people do, because the body is already completely corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is necessary that the cautery be great and small according to the members and joints, according to what you will find in the manners of iron.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After the cure, wash the wound with flour mixed with honey and other remedies until it is healed.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When swelling comes to any member and is treated with medicines, oils, and plasters, but it is not healed, then make a cautery on the member according to its size and smallness; and let the cautery be slightly entering into the flesh of the wound; then cure it with ointments until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And sometimes one does a cautery on the hand and foot and back, at the end of the nerve that moves the member, and thus if it is removed from swelling; and yet no one interferes unless he is knowledgeable about the members and the exits of moving nerves in the body.
de albaras	of abscesses
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" is inflamed, and the medical skill is of no use, then cauterize it with one cautery slightly deep, according to the quantity of fatty tissue, until the pus is removed, and its color changes; then cure with flour mixed with honey and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and blood of cow and blood of almond, each part separately; and mix everything together, and bind it with a cloth, and apply it to the wound until it is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	the cure for chancres by cauterization
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When a chancre comes at the beginning, and you want to arrest it, so cauterize it with the cautery that seems like a circle, all around the perimeter of the chancre.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And yet the wise say that one also makes a cautery in the middle of the chancre; and yet this does not seem to me good, for I fear it will be ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already seen it happen sometimes; and a more direct thing is that it should be cauterized around, with the cautery called "circle", as we said in many cauterizations.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of inflammation that cannot die
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When some person has a disease that is called "adubelati", and it tarries to die or because of the superfluity that it makes or because of the old age of the patient when he is decrepit (that is, too old) and he has little blood, or because of time; and you see it hastening to die: then cauterize him with many small cauterizations piercing; afterwards leave him thus.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For it will hasten to kill.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it piercing all the way through the entire cautery, then heat the cautery with whatever is on hand:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And place your hand in the midst of that disease which is called "adubelati" until the cauterizations have pierced the core, and be such cauterizations that the patient feels them outside in this manner as if the course of the disease were alleviated.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	Afterwards cure him until he is completely healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	the cure for fire by iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another manner of disease is called "corrodens", and it is nothing else than a wasting away of member, for it wastes away the members just as fire consumes dry straw.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this illness in a place that can suffer both cautery and fire, then prepare the cauteries of small and great nails according to what is needed for the place or the illness; after which cauterize all parts until you remove all corruption, so that nothing remains of it, except for everything that is corrupted to be removed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then leave it for three days, and put on the cauterized areas a poultice made with oil as long as the burns of fire are removed, and all corruption is gone.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the ointment treatment has generated flesh.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if you see after three days that healthy flesh does not grow, it is good; and if not, then repeat the cautery on what remains of the corrupted areas.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this remedy has sometimes been used in place of fire cautery by medicine; but nevertheless, fire cautery is of greater aid, and I have already said the cure for medicine aloe in the division: take as much as you need.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of boils that come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Many times it happens that on the feet by default a disease is born which is called "clos" according to our intention, and it is a large gap that hurts the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the fire cauterization of this disease is done in two ways.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	To know it is by fire cauterization and cauterization with hot water.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Fire cauterization is when you heat the cauterizing iron like a quill made of wood, and it is made of good iron to its measure so that it can penetrate the nail from all parts, and there are subtle edges; afterwards, you put it all hot on the nail, and turn your hand entirely around the nail until it reaches the end of the nail; and then leave it like this for three days until it starts to decay; then make a poultice with wild mulberries crushed with oil, and leave the poultice on the entire night, and the nail will fall and be pulled out by its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the joint with oil, anointing it as much as is needed until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if they are converted by a boil on the body, and it happens many times in hands and feet, then you should bring hot water cautery to it; and do thus: take a terra cotta or iron pipe, or a feather from a vulture, and place it on the swelling and the pus-filled area, that is to say, on pustules; and place the pipe so that it encircles all around, then put in a little hot water, and hold your hand well, and press your hand turning so that the edge of the pipe reaches the root of the boil, and then you can find the hot water flowing deep down to the root; and let the patient suffer the burning of the hot water for an hour; then leave it thus, and it will come out with all its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	So treat one after another, until you have reached all those within the body, then cure the humors which cause flesh.
li cure dou trembler	The cure of trembling
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some people tremble due to coldness or nervousness, or quartan fever or another, you should make him have .iiij. cauteries or .iv. on the spine of his back, one cautery between each spine; and one cautery in the weight, and one above the stomach at the olive cautery; if he will leave trembling, and the healths of the cold disease will hasten.
des pustules puans	of foul-smelling boils
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Sometimes appear on the outside of the body, or foul-smelling blisters, that come from great corrupted matter.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	It is necessary at first when they appear to make a fire cauterization on each head of the pustule: a subtle cauterization made of myrtle wood, by which the point may be seized by fire, or of long aristolochia root, or a lentiform cauterization.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And sometimes one cauterizes at the beginning when they appear, according to this manner, and they cannot grow further forward, but are broken off from the superfluous parts that come forth, and are healed; but it is necessary for this to be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Often there is great bleeding from the artery that is cut at the wound that comes to the forefront, or at the incision of the abscess, or at the cautery of the member, and similar things; and it is very grievous to stop.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And yet when this happens to anyone, if you hasten to put your two fingers on the wound of the vein, and hold it tight as long as the blood is calmed under your fingers, and no more flows; then set the olive cauteries in fire, many small and large ones until they are all red; then take one, either big or little according to the wound and its place where the artery runs, and put the cautery on that vein where you hold your fingers, and hold the cautery there as long as the blood is staunched.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it bursts forth when you lift your fingers from the vein, and the cautery has cooled, then take quickly one other of the cauteries that are in the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease to do this one after the other as long as the blood is staunched; and beware that you do not burn the nerve which is nearby, and that no other harm does come upon the patient; and know that when blood flows from an artery, one cannot well stanch it, especially if the artery is large, unless by one of the three ways we have said: or by cautery, or by extraction when it is not yet treated, or by strong binding with thread, or by medicines applied which have power to staunch blood; and let it be tied and restrained accordingly.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who will administer the stanching of blood by binding tightly with cloths or putting burning things on, or similar things, unless it is not effective.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to anyone and he does not have eye or medicine present, then he should put his two fingers on the wound of the vein as we said, and stretch it well until it is staunched above the wound and the vein; and do not move the patient, but keep him moist with cold water often when it is very cold so that the blood may congeal and thicken and be staunched; and make some progress ahead with what he needs of cauteries and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	There begins the second book of surgical cures
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter all diseases in which it is necessary to cauterize with fire or hot medicine, and the ointments and causes and instruments and forms of cauteries; and I have placed that chapter at the head just as far as the end, and I will go on in this chapter by the same way so that you may find more easily what you wish.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And thus, dear son, it is necessary that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of the cauteries, and for that reason it is necessary to be more cautious.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in extracting arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you not to take a foolish risk.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many ways of people come into cures.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	if they come from those who are so afflicted by their illness that they would die quickly due to the discovery of their disease and the greatness of their wickedness; and one should have fear of these.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And from those it happens that someone gives you his opinion, and says: "Wait, I am healed"; and the disease is spiteful.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	It is not fitting that you consent to those who come to you with this manner, but put greater caution in your honor than in your covetousness, and do not act foolishly but wisely about what you are certain of, and about which you can take possession and fame; and use prediction and indication in the cures of your patients so that salvation may be converted; and this will help you to acquire good reputation, and glory, and memory of praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear son, May Our Lord give you good understanding and righteousness, and if you wish to be inspired by the holy inspiration of His hand, Amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Now I have concluded this chapter by dividing it into chapters, according to what is before the chapter on cauteries, which I have divided from the head to the end, so that you may find more easily what you will need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	of the head full of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this disease often comes to children at birth, and when the baby is strained too strongly by the head of the child; and sometimes it comes from a replied cause, which one does not know.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I never saw this disease except in children, and to all that I have seen death hastened; and therefore it seems to me that I should hasten the work of these cures.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw one child whose head was full of water, and the skull grew thicker each day so that it could no longer be sustained; and the moisture became so abundant that it seemed to be dead, and this moisture is assembled beneath the bone above the sphenoid, between the skull and the bone; and the work is such when the moisture is between the skull and the bone, and the abscesses are small, that you cut a gap in the head as wide as two inches, so long as the moisture flows; and see here the shape of the spatumile:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more swollen, and the abscess is larger, then make two incisions in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is below the bone, and the signs that you see are the commissures of the head opened on each part, and the liquid jumps forth when you press with your hand from inside, and this does not respond to you: then it is necessary that you cut three incisions into the head in this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, remove all moisture.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After stitching the tears of cloths and powders, and putting vinegar and oil in them, and leaving it like that for five days; then loosen the bandage, and treat the wound with tents and ointments, and leave the head uncovered, and let the patient eat dry food without moisture until the member is comforted and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way of incision is that you look at where the abscess is opening, and where the liquid is gathering; for sometimes it is in front, sometimes behind, sometimes on the right, and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Cut then where the abscess is opening and the liquid is gathering, and do it according to what you can manage; and beware that you do not cut the artery; and if there comes a flow of blood, so that the patient dies from the decoration of blood and the evacuation of moisture.
de reume	Of rheum (or discharge)
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When it happens to someone a disease called "catarre" in the eyes or at the liver, and the disease is old, and medical treatment does not help, then the last remedy is fire cauterization with which one will sear both arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Therefore, when you cover the wounds, it is necessary for the patient to place their head back; after that, rub the area with a rough cloth as much as the arteries appear, then have the patient pull their neck down to the entire cloth; then look if the vein beats, and the pulsations of one and the other are afterwards the ears, and they are responded; then mark the pulsations by the inch, then cut both sides with a sharp spatula-like tool two parts as much as the skin comes up to the bone, and this should be done by the width of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see, put the spatula under the artery and cut above it, cutting in two like a pair of scissors across.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, the blood will spring forth continuously upwards.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Et if the artery does not open to feeling, then it is necessary that you measure the quantity of the space of three fingers, then sign and fill just up to the bone; and what is needed for the blood to be put out is six cartilages, and by chance a little more or less, according to what the patient can bear, and the replenishment of the artery; then look at the wound: if it remains on the bone point of the sphac, then cut so that apostemes do not come there, then strain the wound and bind, and the ointment cure until it is healed.
de emigrainne	of migraine
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When ancient migraine comes, and acute cataract, due to the moisture of tears and heat in temples and old forgotten habits and similar things, and he has been treated by methods of medical cures and all this does not benefit him, then we extract the arteries of the temples and cauterize them, as we have recounted.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of extracting them is that the patient bends back their temple hairs and feels for the artery that opens in the temple, because it beats well and is somewhat responsive to the touch except in some people who are too cold; and if it is responsive, then extract the patient's neck with some cloths, then rub the spot with a rough cloth, and soak the spot in hot water until the artery becomes manifestly apparent; then take the spatula whose shape is the form:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	Then scrape the skin lightly until you reach the artery, then treat it with pincers, and remove well the threads that are under each part; and if the artery is delicate, then turn it to the point of the thread, then cut off that part according to the quantity of two fingers.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For she is not cut, so does not flow all the blood at once.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And take the blood from 6 to 3 inches; and if the artery is large, it is necessary that you tie it with two strong silk threads in two places, so that no bleeding occurs before the wound has healed and there comes a flow of blood; then cut off the excess that is between the two ties at the same hour, and then, if you see fit, cauterize the area with a cauterizing knife up to the bone until the fingers are cut off; and this is the main work, if the patient does not have fever and is of warm complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For fire cauterization is a help to finish off moisture: that's why it is of greater aid against moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	Or it is necessary for the extraction of arteries that you fill the spot with old cotton and put on well-made tents; and when you take them off, be careful with dry medicines that bring forth flesh and tents, until they are healed; and if without harm to the artery, as long as you work, you hasten to cauterize by fire, or you apply the place of vitriol and strain it in your hand so that the blood is stopped; and if you do not have what is present, put on the spot your debt as much as the blood congeals, and rise the spot with cold water until the bleeding ceases, and be strained as needed; and what is main and lighter in the extraction of the artery is that you cauterize the vein of this fire-cutting knife, but the cutting parts should be well spaced to withstand more heat.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the cuttings are too dense, they retain less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it should have between the two knives one large space, and then when you have marked with ink the two places, and take the hot iron on top so that it reaches up to the bone, and cut off the vein in two places; and be spaced apart between the two fingers because they are not soldered by this cauterization from head to toe; and this is the form of the cauterization:
des larmes	of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.
