Many times a disease called "telul" appears on the nail of the finger, and grows and becomes large over time, until it is something to behold; and therefore it is necessary that you cut it at the beginning, and remove all its fur, then put on the cautery or burning medicine; and if one waits too long to cut it until it is large, take heed if it is hard, with a foul color, poor sensation: do not touch it with iron because it is an enchanted aposteme; for when you cut it some time, great harm comes to the patient; and if the aposteme is of soft touchment, not at all foul colored, and you see that one can completely cut it away, then empty the patient and the doctor without fear, and cure the wound of things drying and constricting.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the nail is cut and cleaned.
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when solutions of continuation come to one of these cartilaginous works, it profits little, more than in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary then to do as follows with each one, if you examine whether the wound is fresh and has all its blood; and then bind the two lips together with a bandage, then treat it until it is healed; and if the lips are already separated on both sides, it is necessary that you scrape away all the parts of their keratin until they heal, then bind the two lips together with a bandage, and strain, and powder on top of powder with dragon's blood, and incense broth; and put on top of the powders a piece of plaster or another plastering substance, and leave it as long as it seems good to it, then treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of the suture is that you assemble the solution: either by needles, as we have said in the suturing of the belly; or by thread, as I have made known.
des apostemes des levres	Of lip abscesses.
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	To many men abscesses have formed inside the lips, hard and resembling grains of millet, larger and smaller; therefore it is necessary that you turn back the lips, and cut each notch, and take out the contents and cut in each part; then apply a poultice to the wound after the incision has been made with vinegar, until the blood is staunched; and then leave the wound open, and cure the wound of things drying until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	Of the flesh of the gums.
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times abscessed flesh appears on the gums, which the ancients call "albulus"; therefore it is necessary that you grasp it with forceps, and cut to its root, and let the blood or pus flow; then put on the wound vinegar or other drying and desiccating powders; and if this flesh returns after the incision, and many times happens, then cut it again and cauterize it: if it does not return after the cautery; and these are the forms of instruments for cutting.
des sordens	Of abscesses.
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes they are gathered at the top of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, scabs that are ugly and rough; and sometimes the teeth are black and yellowish and greenish, as long as corruption comes to the gum, and the teeth stink; therefore it is necessary that you have the patient sit in your hands, and his jaws be in your holy place, and remove the teeth or scabs appearing, until nothing remains; and thus do with the blackness and yellowness, and greenishness and other discolorations, until they are cleaned; and if one removes what is at the first stage, it is good; if not, then begin again on the second day and the third, until you have removed everything; and know that teeth need diverse forms of instruments to remove them, according to what the work shows, because the scraper with which one scrapes away teeth has other forms than he who scrapes between teeth; and these forms and others should be equipped with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you cure the tooth of its pain that you wait to extract it as long as you can, for this should not be done; for it is a very high substance, almost to the point where one has no excuse for pulling.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	When the patient is constrained to go out, it is necessary that you are certain about the tooth aching.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	The patient suffers from pain many times, and thinks it is because of the tooth of Saint Denis, and makes a poultice for the good tooth; and yet the pain does not depart by this, until the evil is removed, for we have already tried it on these saints; and when you are well certain about the tooth aching, it is necessary that you scrape around the tooth with a spatula very carefully to ward off the gum from all sides; then move it to your left or right with subtle tongs in small steps, until it is well separated, then secure the tongs; and have the patient's foot between your knees, and hold it so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extracting the tooth correctly without breaking, and if it does not jump out, then take one of these instruments and insert it inside from each side lightly, and move it as you did first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	Et if the tooth is pierced and bitten, it is necessary that you fill it with cloths, where the holes are; and if it is strained subtly with tweezers, so it does not break while being strained; and it is necessary to work very carefully around the gum for unseating the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And take good care that you do not break it, and leave one part, and reinsert it into the patient through the malicious root causing greater pains than the first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And take care that you do not act like ignorant surgeons who, due to their haste and boldness, sometimes break the tooth, nor bring about what we have described; but they often cause great illnesses through the roots that remain or the tooth that is broken, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is loosened, wash the area with wine or vinegar and sea salt; and if blood comes out, which often happens, use a cloth soaked in vitriol broth; and if this does not help, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of instruments that one uses to extract teeth first are those with long points and large handles, which do not double back when you pull out the tooth; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And have large handles so that they do not bend when pulling, and be made of well-forged iron, and have teeth to keep them from slipping.
de la racine des dens	of the roots of teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains at the track, so it is necessary that you put a moistened cotton cloth on the spot for one or two days.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	Until the flesh is softened, then put in the forceps which are called "algefri", from which the head seems to be like a bone; and are made inside just as a file and that is the shape.
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these forceps, it is necessary that you uncover the entire layer of skin around the root, and put in the instrument called "althali", which is a scraper, by which this is its shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And it should be strong and thick so that it does not break at all, and if the root jumps out with this, that is good; if not, then use all instruments, by which these shapes come next:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you help with this instrument that has two handles, this is its shape:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other tools that are in front of the roots of teeth, and this instrument which seems like great forceps, this is its shape:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And this is the instrument, that it may not break, and knows many instruments of teeth; and also other instruments, which are not counted; and wise and subtle masters find their own instrument by themselves, according to what their works and the disease show them, for there are such diseases where the ancient ones did not teach an instrument due to the diversity of cases, and if one breaks or any other bone, he seeks out the instruments that are needed, which I have told you, and is helped by gestures, this is its shape:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And be strong and well-held to hold the bone, so that it does not slip away, but can be held and removed; and then restore the place with medicines suitable for this, and if there is putridity in the bone, and it is small, then return it to all these instruments:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to its natural place in the body, and the shape is ugly, and especially in young girls, it is necessary that you know if the tooth has grown after the other teeth, and is not in its proper place, and cannot be filed or smoothed: then file it; and if it is uneven with the tooth, take this instrument of which this is its shape, and it resembles a small beak, and be made of iron sharp as a point:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the edge grows gradually day by day due to the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the others; and if it is apparent that one can file it, then use a similar file as this is its shape:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is also like the file with which one makes needles; and in filing the tooth gradually day by day, a little at a time, so that it does not move until it reaches the desired shape; then make it smooth in the end, and if the tooth is too sharp and cuts the tongue, it is necessary to file off the roughness until it is even, so that it does not cut the tongue nor corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the teeth are loose
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the teeth in front are loose, either by percussion or falling out, and the patient cannot press down on what they eat without spitting it out, and you have treated them with restrictive medicines, but this does not work; then they need to be restrained by a thread of gold, for the sons of silver become green and perish, but gold does not change at all; and be the middle thread neither too thick nor too thin, according to the quantity of the space between the teeth; and if you wish to align the teeth, take the thread and tie it double between the two healthy teeth, then put the head between the bad teeth, if there is one or more, until you come out at the healthy tooth on the other side; then re-cover the area up to the point where you started, and strain your hand subtly and slowly, so that it does not move; and be your ligature at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then bend the ends of the thread to a pair of pincers, and assemble them, and reattach between two healthy teeth, and set it so that it does not hurt the tongue; and then leave it thus tight as long as it can remain, and if it comes undone or the threads rot, tighten with another thread; if it remains and serves like this for its entire time, and this is the form of the teeth and the figure of the arrangement of two healthy teeth and two molars, just as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls out, then put it back in its place, gradually and carefully, just as we have said; and do not meddle with it unless you are a skilled and patient person, and at times make the shape of a whalebone tooth, and put it in the place where there is a deficiency, and strain it on, just as we have said, and remain and serve thus for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cover the link of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	Sometimes this string comes from under the tongue or natural fibers, which one is born with; or by accident of a healed wound; and the work is such that you do to the mouth of the patient, and have their head in your healthy one, and lift up the tongue; then bend the nervous thread from the wide one, until the tongue is loosened from its dwelling, and if there is hardness or knot, it's due to a sudden wound, so put the bandage and bend the wide one that bond; and beware that the opening is not too deep by fontanelle, for the artery which is below; and when you have done this, then lift up the rose-colored and gentle water, or cold water, and place it under the tongue a linen tent; and let the patient sleep each night so that the wounds do not heal.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if there is bleeding, put on the glassy leaden dressing; and if the blood flows, cauterize it with the slow fire cautery, which is good for that; then treat with another treatment until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if you see it of fusse color or black or hard, and the patient does not feel it, then do not touch it, for it is a chancre; and if it is declining to blenchor, and there is moisture, throw on unguent, and make a gentle poultice with a spatula, and deliver from one side and the other; and if the blood flows at your work, put vinegar on it until it is stopped, then return to your work until you have treated all thoroughly; then lift up the linen cloth and cure it with other treatments until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	of abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes there comes within the throat a growth that is called "godath", and it is properly called the II almonds; and when you cure them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, beware: if it's an abscess of small sense and dull color, do not touch with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it's red and the root is thick, do not touch with iron, also for the bleeding; but leave it until it's dead, and then you will cut it off, or it would break apart on its own; and if it's of white color again, and the root is fine, prepare your instrument to cover, but look first to see if the abscess has cooled down and is calmed.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Put the patient to sit before the sun, and his legs be in good tone, and have him open his mouth and take the tongue between his hands, and press it under all the instrument, which is the form; and it should be of silver or subtle copper like fine knives:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Press the tongue to all this instrument and you see the abscess, then take the needle and the stick in the almond, and draw it out above as much as you can; and do not touch anything with the cloth, then cut the instrument, by which the form appears, as if it were some force; and though the head is crooked, one side to the other, and are very sharp, and made of iron or bone.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, then use pincers, by which the form appears:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And be cutting from one side and the other; and when you have cut one of the almonds, then cut the other in the same manner, and after the incision, gargle the patient with hot water, and cool and easy, and if bleeding occurs, then gargle the patient with warm water, or cooked apple skins, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the bleeding stops; then apply a cure until it is healed; and sometimes other abscesses arise in the throat than the two almonds, so cut them then in the same way as the two almonds similarly.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman with an abscess that was born inside her throat, to wit, the small sense abscess; and I had well closed all the throat, so that the woman could not expire because the passage was blocked, and could not eat or drink, and would have died if she remained thus for one day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so swollen that it had forced its way out through both holes of the nose.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I hastened then, and put a poultice on one nostril, then I drained the pus, and let out a great deal of discharge; then I refilled the other nostril with the poultice, and opened the mouth and pressed the tongue; after that, I put the poultice on the abscess, and cut part of it away, and only a little blood came out; and thus the passage in the woman's throat was unclogged, and she began to drink water and then wine, and did not stop cutting away at that abscess for a long time; and the abscess kept growing back again, and filling up the space I had emptied, until it became very large; then I treated it and cauterized it inside the throat: thus it grew no more; and I left those parts, and only God knows what happened to them after me.
de l’uve	of the vein
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When it rises from the eye and it is inflamed and it is long, so it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is below a growth and rounded, so it is called "uvula".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not benefit, and you see that the pus-filled abscess is appeased, and it is subtle, so it is necessary to scrape it; and that which is rounded assembled and is not long; and it is sanguine or of a fusse color or black, so it is necessary to avoid cutting into it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	Because there is great danger on the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	It is necessary then, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, to cause the patient to sit before the sun, and press the tongue onto the instrument of which we made a record here before; then insert the onychium into the eye, and draw it down, and scrape with the two instruments that I said in the incision of the two almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you do not cover too much more than the superfluity that is outside of the natural term; for if you cover more, it will grieve at the voice and at the word; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of II amandres, and cure it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear to cover, you should use cunning at the cauterization of their sense of fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery is sharp as an edge.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And it is that the patient places their head on your shoulder, and then presses their tongue to the instrument which we have said in the chapter of cautery, and confesses with a sharp, living coal, so that it is neither too thick nor too thin; and in employing this instrument, by which there is the form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let the patient's head be covered with a cloth or a man put the medicine, as the hairs of a comb, and place the instrument on all the medicine above the vein; and have the patient lie on their side so that saliva and mucus flow from their mouth into the medicine, but not down to the throat and wound. Then keep your hand on all the medicine and press it on the vein for the quantity of half an hour, until you see it turn white and the medicine's blistering is appeased; and if you see, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and soak the cotton in the medicine, and put the instrument in a tube above the cotton on the cane, so that the cotton sits on top of the vein; and do this often until the cautery is complete, then let it dry, and wait for three or five days. And if you need to start again with the medicine's cautery, start again, and after the cautery, remove the surrounding area around the vein with a cloth wrapped in butter, and purify all that is around the medicine; and be washed with cold water, and be cured through gargling until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is more safe than incision, and cauterization; if it is cured through fumigation according to this manner, take calament, ysope, origanum, rue, camomille, and avronne, and similar herbs, and assemble all or some of them in one pot, and put a little water in it, and make it boil; and let the pot be well glazed with hot earth, and have an instrument inside shaped like this:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And let it be of silver or of gold, and let the one of the keys be inserted into the mouth of the patient until the vapor rises to the ear through the tube, until the ear is numbed; afterwards it often recurs, until the ear is dry, and take care that you do not do this at the beginning of the swelling of the abscess hot, for many things happen there; nor do anything but at the decline of the hot abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, take a tube and put a hen's quill inside it, so that the patient's mouth does not have too much heat; for the quill of the hen does not allow the vapor to weigh heavily on the mouth, and it is good care together with salvation.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times it happens that something is stuck in the throat or spine of a fish, or nothing at all; therefore it is necessary that you do what you can see, and press the patient's tongue to the sun on the entire instrument, so that you see how things go; and what does not open up and remains stuck in the throat, it is necessary that you make the patient vomit before the meat is cooked in the stomach; by chance, if the thing opens up through vomiting; or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of naval, or a lettuce root, or a dry crumb; and tie the sponge with a thread, and then have it pass through; and when it comes out, it will be stuck, and then you will pull on it harder; and if it does not come out from what we have said, take an instrument of lead according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instruments be curved at the head so that it can enter the throat more easily, and have the head in high lift; and take care not to touch the epiglote, lest all go wrong, nor push the bone inside; and move cautiously that the patient pushes the instrument, because it may move or the thing is awkward; then push down, or pull forward to all the instrument evenly, until it is pulled out.
de la sansue de la gorge	Of the sweat of the throat.
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	At no time is bloodletting medicine, as I said in the division, by the cure of medicines; and when that does not help, then look into the patient's throat at the sun, then press his tongue onto the instrument which I told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the sweat, then take it away with all small needles or fine forceps that are suitable for this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if this doesn't work, then take a braided cord, and tie it around the patient's neck, then heat the iron rod at the end of the cord, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient is troubled by water all day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take the full cup of cold water, and make the patient spit it out, and then swallow without swallowing again, and move their head often; and as soon as the sweat feels the water, let them fall asleep.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if she doesn't fall asleep as we said, then suffumigate the patient with assafoetida at the instrument that I mentioned in the fumigation of the eye; do this many times, for she will sleep without stirring.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the manner of fumigation is that you take a pot where it has charcoal fires, and the pot be covered with a perforated cloth in the middle, and in that hole be the key to the instrument; then throw your fumigation, and the patient puts the end of the pipe in their mouth, and closes their mouth so that the smoke does not escape but comes just to the sweat; and the sweat will now fall, and if it does not fall, then continue the fumigation many times; and let the patient be thirsty, and eat salty things and sweets, and do not drink water; and then it is necessary for it to come forth by this governance.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument with which you treat the sweat is such that when you can see it, it resembles curved pincers for moving into the throat; and has a resemblance to a bee's stinger, and it has a spiky surface like lime, so that whatever it takes, it cannot let go; and behold its form:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapters on abscesses.
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Many kinds of abscesses are, according to what is remembered hereafter in this book, and they differ in their perforation and size; and there are two manners in which one is the same in appearance, and that which holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second manner is for the bones that are at the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscesses of the head are different from those of the foundation, and the abscesses of the fatty tissue are different from those that come together in joints, and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if there are abscesses that one should not pierce, until the bowels are mature according to their completion; and if there are such that it is necessary to pierce when they are dry, and do not die according to their completion, as those abscesses that are beneath joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come beneath joints, and one leaves it until it is rotting all around, by chance the ligaments and nerves of the joint are corrupted, which is the cause of contraction in that member.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	Or the abscess is beneath the principal member, and if you delay perforation until it is rotten, it will harm the principal member; or if it is at the foundation, then one should pierce it as soon as it is dead; and it does not behoove that you pierce a dry abscess without digestion being completed, except for that which is at the foundation, lest it burst forth and become a fistula, and cannot heal in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary that you know the time of the perforation of the abscess which is dead according to its completion, and this is when the pain is subsiding, and the departures of fever, and the decrease of pain and redness, and the quieting and settling of the head of the abscess, and other signs; and it is necessary that you make the perforation dependant on the location of the abscess, and where it appears more; and be the perforation of long duration in the body, and if the abscesses are at the hands or feet, or in joints, and near nerves and arteries, and in all equal places where there is no pain.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those who ache, by consequence of that member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when abscesses are in the skin hardened, so it is best that you leave the puncture until it is confirmed in completed digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce it before that, the body will be lengthened by the venom from it, and is filled with great stench of filth; and perchance harden the lips and deepen those parts of it.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if there is any abscess that is pierced according to the breadth of the body, according as the members may need it.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And it is necessary that you make small incisions in small abscesses, and large incisions in large abscesses, and many cuts according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses where it is necessary to cut out the core, and cover; when it has become as worn-out rags, and is exhausted, then do as one does with babies: and if there are those that are split in three angles, and if there are those which are covered like the leaf of myrtle, as abscesses of the armpits; and if there are such where you make a round cut, and other cuts and similar covering.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Cil who have not a head, as an abscess on the surface of the skin, it is necessary that you pierce it thoroughly; and it is necessary when the abscess is large, and has gathered a great deal of pus, and you pierce it, if you do not pull out all the pus in one hour, but pull out part of it; then stop the abscess until the next day, then pull out something else above it; do this many times gently, as much as is necessary, until all the pus has come out; similarly if the patient is of weak virtue, or a woman bearing, or small children, or old men decrepit.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the pulse beats quickly sometimes with the issue of pus, so that by chance the patient dies, and you are not aware.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then therefore, carefully read this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, if the wound is open, and look to see if the abscess's wound is small; and if it's a clean cut, then bind it with linen or old cotton cloth; and if it's large abscesses, and there are many pits, then it is necessary that you place one tent on each so they come together; and if you have cut into the abscess a piece of skin, and you have wrapped it around, then it is necessary that you fill it with old cotton or linen cloth without moisture, and tie it until the third day; then remove it, and care for it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if bleeding occurs at your work, then administer cold water and vinegar, and damp cloth, and place it on the bleeding spot repeatedly.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the bleeding persists, then administer governance and care, and the powders that I have said to use in this book, and if it's in the time of winter, and the wound or abscess is very inflamed, then you should put on wet tents and cloths soaked in wine and hot oil; and if it's in summer, and the wound is fleshly, then you should put on cloths soaked in water and oil, or in cold wine, until the third day, as we have said; and then remove the abscess and apply a poultice to cure it, as needed, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And it is necessary to know universally in the treatment of abscesses: for I have told you how one should proceed before treating abscesses, and see here the chapter.
des soros	of boils
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Where small abscesses come from the head, and they are like little nests that we find in fabrics, just as a sparrow's nest is woven with threads, and there are many similar ones.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are fat and such places where there is moisture also like pimples; and if there are such places that are hard and stony to cut into, and there is no doubt if the artery does not go against.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the works of cutting are such that you try out all the instruments which are called "entromissoires", from which the form comes afterwards, whatever thing it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, then let them make an incision above the long one.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is empty, then scrape away without leaving any skin that contains that moisture, for it returns again if you leave anything; then dip cotton in Egyptian oil, if present; if not, in water and vinegar, and fill the wound, and let it stay until the next day; and those who remain of the night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then rewrap the cotton, just like before, on the second day, and the third, until you are certain it does not remain at night; then treat the wound with ointment as needed, until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess is not large, then cut it according to this form, from long; and pull out your probes, and scrape off all sides, and put all your care in pulling away from the skin where it lies; and if the artery resists you, do what I have told you afterwards.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also do this with the abscess if it is pustular, and to cut and cure as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the cutting on the pustular abscess and the moist one is lighter, for they are full of blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if some of these abscesses or pustules are dry and have no moisture, and among those abscesses that I cut open on the head of an old woman; and I found the abscess just like a stone, rough and white, and could not break it; and if one had been made to burst, it would have made a wound like a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses coming from the head, more than those that come to the heads of children and roots of ears, the opening should always be at its most dependent place in order for pus to issue forth; and it should be cured as is fitting.
des scrophules	of scrofulas
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times these abscesses occur in the neck and under the armpits and in the groin, and sometimes they come elsewhere in the body, and are many and are intertwined with one another.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofula is properly located within its own fold, just as the nodes and abscesses of the head, as we have said; and similar instances of these scrofulas are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and also there are evil ones who do not wish to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	Then when you see one with good condition for cutting, and it looks like the color of the body, is smooth on all sides, and is not inflamed around the neck or artery or vein, and is not deep; then it is necessary that you cut it open from above, and scrape each part, and make the two lips of the wound at the edges, as we have said in abscesses of the head; and do it little by little, and be careful not to cut the nerve or vein, nor let the spatula get stuck, so that your hands escape, and you don't cut anything you shouldn't.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or artery, and it does not let you operate, then put in the wound vitriol poultice, or some powders that stop blood, and close the wound; and leave it so that the abscess is calmed, and the wound becomes soft, and begins to rot.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the blood is stopped, then return to your work, until you complete it; and then examine whether there remain any small scrofulae, if you cut them and remove them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein at the root of the scrofula, then it's not necessary to cut that scrofula at its root, but tie it with a double strong thread and let it fall off by itself, without harm; then bathe the wound in old Egyptian cotton ointment, and then treat it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cover the entire scrophule, it is necessary that you bring together the two lips of the wound and sew them up now, then there will be no remaining superfluity due to the greatness of the scrophule.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	it is necessary that you understand to cover the root of it, and pull strongly, and sew it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scrophules that retain superfluity, perforate there where it appears more; and the perforation is done thus as was said earlier, in dependence, then tentatively with ointment and similar things, so that what remains of the corruption corrupts it; and when the wound is well cleansed, apply ointment on top of the flesh until it is healed.
de squinance	of squinancy
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients said and spoke of the cutting of the throat; but I never saw anyone in our land who did it, and that is the writing of their word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	To those who have squinancy, it is necessary that the opening of the throat, which is called "epiglote", be removed; and one does not provide assistance through these things, because all the veins and the pores of the patient are hot in the mouth, or in the throat, or in both armpits.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the pore, it is necessary to cut the epiglote in order to avoid the peril that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	Therefore, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, it is necessary that we cut it below three circles or four small cuts across its width, between the two circles or according to the size of the opening of the syphac, not in the cartilage; and this way is suitable for the section of the epiglottis, since there is no flesh, and the vessels are long and deep.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is fearful, it is necessary that he stretches the skin of the throat to the entire neck, then cuts the leather so far as it comes to the chin; and avoids the vessels of blood, if you see anything, and then closes the syringe, just as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the section of the vein at the chin which bursts forth through the torn place and due to the lack of voice; and leaves the wound open for a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed when one doubts strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound of the flesh, and sew it all up without the cartilage; then administer medicines that cause flesh to grow, until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	On does not make this just so long as the throat is completely swollen, and the patient is judged to be dying, and death approaches.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then one should close the epiglote because the patient cannot breathe, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is guarded from death; and therefore the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the malady of the disease has passed, and it passes in three days or four. And then they commanded to sew up the wound and cure it, until it was cured; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a young lady took the knife, and stuck it in her throat, and cut off part of the channels of the womb; and I was called to cure her, and found her as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound and found the blood that was issuing from it, and I knew that she had not cut her throat nor conducted anything except the throat, and the veins were flowing out through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hastened, and sewed the wound, and cured her until she was well; and it happened to the young lady that she lost her voice, and then returned to her normal state; therefore I say that in cutting into the epiglottis one should not be afraid.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called "hernia of the throat", and it is a great abscess in the color of jasper, and it is very common in women; and it occurs according to two manners: natural and accidental; or if it is natural, there is no deceit.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental is according to two manners, by which one resembles fat in us, and the other manner resembles an abscess that comes from a vessel; and there should be fear, and it is not right to do anything except on that one which is small, and test it and search all the interior: if you find it like I say, and it cannot be moved by any means, so cut it off, as one cuts fat, and treat it with all its folds, if there are none; and search well everything, and cure it as it should be, until it is whole and perfect.
des nous	of the nose
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	Many ways are ours, of which I will say all the likenesses; and now it is necessary that I say all the difference that is between our joint and its place.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that exit is heat and feverish, as long as the ebullition has not passed, and the putrefaction is completed; then the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With the joint there is no heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains a sac, which is its own bag and is according to the color of the flesh, and begins also like a blister, and becomes large; and they are according to two likenesses, either fatty or moist, and much color as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the cure of the nose, that you examine and inquire first through all the instrument which is called "interstice", according to what its form will be or the chapter which comes afterwards.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the manner of inquiring into abscesses is that you take or more moist place than you find in the abscess, and turn your two pots and pots, until you know that the instruments have pierced the core, then as it should be according to the size of the abscess; then extract the foreign body, and take care not to force it.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If moisture congeals, whatever its color may be, do it as I have said for other abscesses; and if afterwards the interstice does not bring forth moisture, know that it is fat, so then do it in a cross pattern, and take hold of the pincers, and lightly scrape off each part and guard the skin where it lies until you can draw it out safely with the needle; and if you cannot draw it out safely, cut it into pieces such that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if nothing remains, then the wound will recur many times; and if a small part remains and the blood still grieves, use corrosive powders on the wound, apply pressure to the wound, and place warm soothing poultices on the abscess, and cure it with other remedies until it is healed; and if the flesh is large, then cut off the two lips of the wound, and cure what remains of the skin.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the vein beats against you or some other thing that is contrary, and you hasten and apply the lead of vitriol dissolved, and let it be so for two days or three, until the wound purifies, and repose the ebullition of blood; then return to cutting what remains of the nose.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Here is the translation:
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The forms of tumors are of many similarities, as you see here: great, medium, and small; and if there are tumors that have two shapes in three ways; and if there are tumors that have three shapes, and they are also in three ways; and if there are tumors that have two shapes, and a tumor with only one shape, and they are in three ways; and all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The heads of these things are cut, and some do not cut as much as one side, so that one removes the flesh, because one does not touch the vein or nerve; and among these interlopers are the stitches sewn in threads, so that the patient is not aware of the opening of abscesses; and they come in three ways: great, small, and medium, as you see; and one does not use them excessively except on charnut places, such as legs, arms, breasts, and shoulders, and similar places; and sometimes one makes another small instrument, resembling thread used for sewing, according to this form, so that blood is staunched.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and one puts it sometimes in the location where veins and arteries are healed completely, and sometimes according to this great form;
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Breasts of some men become inflamed when they begin to be corrupted, as long as they seem like woman's breasts; and remain swollen and inflamed, and whoever wants to cure them, it is necessary to follow this form until 2.b. up to 7.g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Then scrape away the fat, and fill the wound with medicine releasing fat, then bring together the two lips of the wound by stitching, and care for it until it is healed; and if the breast droops down, and becomes worn out due to its size as in women, then make incisions in two parts above, through two similar notches; so that one holds onto the other at the end of each, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form from .b. up to .g.; then scrape away the skin that is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and apply what we have said about stitching and powders, and what is necessary for the cure, until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or the incision is not yet fully made, because the patient does not want to rest, or due to bleeding, then you must fill the wound with moistened cotton in corrosive oil; and leave it until it has soaked up the remaining fat, then care for it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come from under the armpits are kinds of hard scrofulae or those with nodules, and some contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those who contain moisture need to be cut according to this form, from line .b. to line .g.
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus that is in the abscess has been emptied, then fill the wound with old cotton and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and care for it with oil suitable to this purpose until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is of the same kind as scrofulae, then cut it as we have said in incisions for scrofulae, and if the wound yields pus, then apply cauterization as we have said before.
