Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This illness is called in our land "vakirir", and it is a pain that comes to some members, and can move from member to member; and I have seen what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and then, about an hour later, I saw it rise again, just like a worm on the shoulder, more quickly than anything, like quicksilver when it flows from one place to another; the pain left that place and settled in the shoulder, and then a little while after it ran all over the body, until it came to the other arm; then she told me that it was turning back around the body, just as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was very surprised how she moved thus from member to member, for I had never seen this disease in this way before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	However, I had wanted to see many others who had well moved pain from place to another, but I did not see this in the woman; and I thought that it was because the woman had a dry body, and her veins were uncovered, and so appeared that windiness constrained; and do not appear according to this reason to those who are delighted, and who have moist bodies and responsive veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	When you see the patient being cured of this disease, and they feel that pain, if it opens up as we have said, quickly bind above and below; then strike above until the swelling compels to return to its place; cauterize the place; and if you do not see it with your own eyes, cure it with what constrains the swellings, such as fetid pills and serpent pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the places in the body where they fall.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of arrows is that there are those with large points, small ones, and barbed ones, and those with two angles, and those with tongues, and those with pieces; and one that hits a member can hit in two ways: either in the principal member so it breaks, such as head, heart, liver, pancreas, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it falls then in any place of these members, and the sign of death that I will tell you afterwards warns you: so you must beware of extracting this arrow, for many die after; and when this bad sign does not warn you at all, and the arrow is not far out, then take hold of it and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the brain is when the arrow hits and pierces the bone, and the flesh that is above the brain starts to swell and becomes discolored and inflamed; and in the mouth, tongue turns red and there is convulsion and mixing of understanding; and vomiting of bile; and perhaps it is without sense of smell or hearing; and perhaps the speech and voice are impaired; and a foul-smelling white discharge like pimples appears from the wound, and in the same way as if boiled flesh; and if this sign warns you, then hold off from treating the wound, and take out the arrow if it's not too deep.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of the arrow when it falls on the heart is that it is near the left breast, and feels as if it were stuck in something hard, not empty; and by chance the arrow moves just like the hairs, and there is black blood in court, and comes with coldness and cold sweat, and fainting: know then without doubt that death draws near.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow that strikes the liver is that without foam it bursts forth from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient's face turns color, and he sighs high and seeks cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow hits the covering of the ribs, it is beneath the small bones; and pours out great pain and great suffering, and sighs; and all the muscles of the shoulders tremble.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow hits the stomach, perhaps something from undigested food bursts forth from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow hits the belly, and bursts forth a small amount of pus through the intestine route, there is no hope for the cure, nor for the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow hits the bladder, and the urine bursts forth and comes out, and the patient feels very painful: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the face and the neck and the throat and the shoulders and the shoulder blade and the spine of the back and the nape and the hips and the knees and the feet, and similar members, are safe according to many dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you what happened to me, so that you may do likewise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to one at home that an arrow fell into the nose at the root of the night; I tried to remove it and pulled it from the other side under the fatty fold of the ear, and he was healed without numbness.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And I pulled out an arrow that had fallen into the fatty fold of the eye under the paper-thin skin, and the arrow was bent back, and I could not grasp it except for the point towards where it was stuck, and the arrow was as long as a Turkish bow, so light that one could lift it with their ears; the boy was healed, and no bad event came to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And pull out an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabian with ears: I saw the beard-ends, and pulled it out slowly until I pulled it out, and the Christian became well.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And pull out an arrow from the man, that was stuck in his belly, and thought he was dying; and then after he had passed 30 days, his condition didn't change; I cut above the arrow, and wove it in, and pulled it out, and there was no bad accident.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if the arrow fell on a man's back, and the wound was closed above; and the arrow remained inside him, and didn't change his natural disposition, nor found any harm in any of his natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And saw another man, to whom an arrow fell on his face, and the wound was closed; and remained in this way without suffering great pain; and many others similar.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And draw an arrow to the man of princes the king, who was struck in the neck, and was slightly declining to the right part; and the arrow was entirely stopped I was summoned to the treatment after it had been stuck for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I searched for it with great subtlety and did not find it; and he felt a pricking and pain under his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow I applied a poultice to the wound attracting and digestive, because the flesh did not swell; and the arrow's head appeared.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I applied the poultice for many days and the wound healed above, and the patient remained thus for a long time until he felt the arrow one day inside his neck; and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I applied medicine with a corrosive agent to the wound for several days, until it was open and exposed, and I tried to treat it, and felt the tip of the arrowhead that was lodged at the site; then I inserted into the opening of the wound with that medicine, so long as the head of the arrow appeared clearly visible; and it survived beyond four months, and then became inflamed so much that I put in tongs, and pulled it out from one side and the other, but it would not come out; then I did not cease to subtilize and ingeniously devise various instruments, until I grasped the arrowhead with well-made tongs, as described at the end of this chapter.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the doctor judged that the cartilage of the nose could not be restored; I restored it then, and the wound was healed, and the patient was completely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Or that's said the quality of the extraction of some arrows, so that you put your cure on what I did not say, for books cannot grasp everything; but wise masters have learned well about small things and present needs, find new work and new instruments, in the descent of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not come from members or where they are stuck except in two ways: either by the way they enter or by another part; and that which jumps forth from there where it enters is an arrow entering into the flesh, and sometimes now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not jump now, so leave it until the flesh around is ripe and the opening is clear; and similarly if it is stuck in the bone and cannot come out, so leave it thus for some days and move each day; and then it jumps, and if it does not jump, so bore through all subtlety, until the skin around is stretched, and then deal with it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	If the arrow is stuck in the skull of the head and goes just to one of the ventricles of the brain, and some of the accidents that I have mentioned occur in the patient: do not pull it out immediately, but let it stay equal for several days, because if the arrow comes close to the sacral bone, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is stuck only in the bone and does not come close to the sacral bone, and the patient remains some days without a bad accident, then it is expedient to pull out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is stuck deeply and cannot come out, I will administer tarers around, as I have told you; then treat the place until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is lodged in the body and cannot be seen, so it pierces through all the tent; and if you can feel it, then pull it out with some suitable instrument; and if you cannot due to the tightness of the wound, and the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone or nerve or vein, then file down the wound until it is large enough; and pull out the arrow if you can, and if it has ears attached to what holds it in place, cut away the flesh that is stuck for two parts as far as you can, and then break or bend the ears of the arrow, so that you can pull it out; and be subtle that you do not break the arrow, lest you pull it out more grievously.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you can't all at once, then leave it until the flesh around is melted, and then pull it out, for the extraction will be eased.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the bleeding makes you uneasy, then do as we have said in its chapter; and beware of incision on the nerve and vein, and think how you can safely draw out the arrow either quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and put the patient according to the shape they were when the arrow hit them, for that is the greatest help that there is, and if you cannot, then do as the sign shows you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from the other side, or if it has lodged anything in there, or the skin is swollen where you can see or feel alarmingly: then cut above, until the forceps can grasp, and then pull it out: if it jumps now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is stuck in the bone, then turn your hand roundly, until it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot come out, then leave it there and start extracting again until it comes out; and if the arrowhead is stuck, then cover it with all the head; and if the arrowhead falls, and you must administer a poultice, then apply an instrument with a smooth part, so that the point of the arrow enters into the hair of the instrument; and then push forward, and if the arrowhead is pulled out, then insert the instrument at the entering point to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is stuck, so you should cut away all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, then treat the wound as it needs to be treated.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow hits or falls on the head, belly, bladder, or ribcage, and it is close, and you can cut into it, then cut there; and take care not to cut the vein and nerve, then pull it out, then cut the wound as needed; and treat it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps with which one treats arrows are similar to a bird's beak, and see here the shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many kinds: great, small, and little ones, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the arrowhead is also like the plumage of a bird, to push against the tip of the arrow, as it is shaped:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of the forceps for pushing and for pulling out if it is like this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of common veins of the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	Of the veins by which one purifies oneself there are 31, and of these 16 are on the head, to wit: two batons that are after the ears, which are called "herbech"; and two arteries that appear in two temples; and two veins that are in two corners of the eyes, which are called "aspires"; and the vein that is in the middle of the forehead; and the vein that is on the crown of the head; and two guides that are in the neck; and two veins that are above the lips of the mouth, and these are the veins that are called "augeherich"; and two veins that are below the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins commonly used for bleeding are two in each arm: one is the cephalic, which is located on the left side and is called by common people "the vein of the head"; and the median is called "faste", which is composed of the cephalic and basilic, and is called by common people "the vein of the heart"; and the basilic is on the right side, and is called by common people "the vein of the belly"; and it is above the foreskin, and it is that one used for bleeding, which opens manifestly above the pouch.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the saphenous vein is the one that is between the ulnar and radial, and it has two branches; and in the leg and foot are three veins: one is below the pouch of the left side, and the second one is at the ankle on the right side; and the vein called "nesse" which is in the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg are three veins below those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: and is that the patient stretches his neck so that the two veins appear clearly; and feels the pulse below his thumb, and then signs off; then raises the key above the vein to the height of his thumb index, and pushes the lancet below, and raises the vein high, and cuts it as you have done in two other veins, and makes a incision according to your necessity; then releases the patient, and puts his thumb on the vein for an hour, then puts cotton on; and then ties it up tightly, and leaves it until it is healed; and we have spoken of its cutting and extraction, and of the beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The bleeding from the vein of the forehead is worth as much as the bleeding from the cephalic vein in old diseases of the face and in migraines, and in redness; and the quality is that the patient stretches his neck by twisting, until the vein appears; then take the instrument called "fossor", which is formed thus:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the point on the vein, and press down with your hand or something else, and let the blood flow out according to the quantity you see; then loosen the patient's neck and tie the vein so it is secure and no more than a small flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not necessary that the gashes be too deep; and let the blood flow across, for the bone is pressed, and by chance break the gash when it is fine.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The bleeding from the two veins that are in both eyelids helps greatly with boils, and with itching, and with redness, and with inflammation of the eye, and with diseases of the face; and the quality of their bleeding is that the patient stretches his neck by twisting without any binding, just as before; then bleed, and let the blood flow be about one span long, about a finger's breadth wide, for there is no flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the gashes are fine, by chance it breaks; then make sure to stop the bleeding as much as you need to, and then tie on a cloth, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The blood of the vein of the nose is so valuable for agha, and for sudden fever, and for facial diseases, such as migraine and redness that comes on the face, and especially when it is old; and the qualities of the blood are that the patient tightens their throat, then strains their nose with their left hand, and takes the subtle flame long and puts it in the space between the two nostrils, for the vein does not open well there, and the blood will begin to flow now; and do not go too far up, and let the blood flow according to your need, then bind it a night, for it is soon restored; and this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The blood of the two gullies is very helpful for constriction of the brain, and for beginning of menstruation, and for many diseases, and for dropsy, and for corroisons, and for herpes, and eczema; and the qualities of the blood are that the patient tightens their throat above one and the other, as we have said; and let the master be standing on the head of the patient, and the patient sit in a siege, then take the vein of the long one slightly wide, then pull out the blood temperately, or so long as is necessary; then do the other side in the other vein, then release the lien, and strain out the veins moderately, that the patient does not strangle; and let it be until morning, when the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	of the healing of books
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The vein of the veins above the lips so helps in bleeding in the mouth, and in corruption of gums, and splits in lips, and around.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the quality of healing is to have the patient sit before you, and strain their neck as I said; then turn the tongue, and look at the two veins, one on the right side and the other on the left, and recognize them by what they are black, and by what surrounds them with small black lines: cut both then, and if you don't know them, and you're in doubt, so cut the thicker of each part, and do the same for the two veins that are above and below, because it's the same method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of the healing below the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The healing of the veins that are below the tongue helps after the healing of the cephalic one, and it's at the constriction of the throat, and with the diseases of the eye, and with the diseases of the mouth; and the quality of the healer is to have the patient sit between your hands in the sun, and lift the tongue, and look below each side for a black vein: heal both then, and don't go too deep, because beneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	Veins of the throat which are commonly used for bleeding are healed in two manners: either piercing them with a broad mirthin flame, or an olive-green subtle one such as cutting trenchers, and it is called "anesil"; and they are broad and subtle according to the breadth and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the fine gash is very renowned, and is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is necessary to open the thick-veined veins that are full of large apparent blood, and which contain large and troubled blood; and this is the form of the olive-green flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more subtly pointed, and is for bleeding the subtle veins where there is subtle yellowish blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The vein of the basilica, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases that are below the throat, and in the neck, and in the breast, and in the belly; and it is necessary for the surgeon to bleed profusely and to beware of the artery that is below.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if he cuts the artery, and a flow of blood comes forth, then it is necessary to staunch it, as I said; and one should not pierce the flame, but cut as with anesil.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilica does not open clearly, then you must extract it, and change another one; or you want any part of it, or you suture in place of it the vein within the arm: it opens clearly; and cut at the flame anesil, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you want to know the location of the wound, then it is necessary that you extract the arm, so that you touch the location until you know the pulse; then mark the location with anointing oil, and bind the arm, and cut the vein at the flame anesil; and be careful not to hit the artery when you see the location swelling, for it is the artery: avoid this.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it coming out above like a child's urine, and the blood is red and fine, know that it is blood from the artery: hasten then, and place your finger on top for a long time, then remove your finger if the bleeding stops, which often happens; bind the arm, and leave it so, and do not move the patient until he is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the bleeding is not stopped, and it gapes open, and medicine is not present to you, then cut the artery if it opens up, for the head of it will retract; and stop the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And take a husk of fistic, and cut it, and take one half and tie well just to the other day; if the wound stays still, that's good; if not, then heal it with powders that stop blood as we said; and the stoppage is not grievous in many dispositions due to the small size of the wound, and the power of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The vein of the vein in the mixture is so helpful that it treats blood from the head above and the body below, because it is composed of basilic and cephalic, as we said; and it is necessary for the physician to be wary of the nerve that is below, and if he pushes too deep, he will find the nerve, and it will swell and the bleeding will be grievous, and by chance may not heal; and this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in some men due to its subtlety, then you must use the healthy vein of the instrument; and stop the nerve at your power.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, then cut it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The wound of the cephalic artery helps so much that it attracts blood from the head and helps the eyes; and it is necessary to bleed at the sharp point of the olive or myrtle flame, for it is the most safe of all veins, because there is no nerve nor artery below.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	However, it is necessary to seek the lighter place, and not disturb anything if you must do it the first time, and then begin again; and by chance, some men's places swell up, when you have to do it the first time, but it does not cause any disturbance.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the vein is according to your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you should know about bleeding is that it is done only to preserve health and to forestall impending illnesses; and let the bleeding be done in one of the three veins that are there: namely, cephalic, facial, and basilic; and one should bleed at the beginning of Lent, and in autumn and winter after meals, when the sign of repletion appears; and one should bleed on the first or third day, after two or three hours of the day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The sick person who is treated for illnesses has no fixed time determined, but only when the need arises by day or night, at all hours and in all times; and it is not necessary to heal children until they are 14 years old, nor a woman carrying less than four months' child until the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Nor should the elderly who have passed 60 years not be cauterized.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when someone wants to be healed, in whatever way it may be, it is necessary that they loosen their intestines with a light enema if they have many retained phlegms, so that the veins do not attract superfluous substances which are harmful to the main members; nor does one become healthy who is too full of meat, or drunk, until they are better, or dropsical; and after suffering from colic passion, vomiting, and bowel evacuation, and frequent attendance on a woman, travel, watching, and sleeping, and all that is contrary to nature, or due to the arm or body; then purify the humors if the blood is thick, through food, drinks, and medicines, if you have the power; then enter into bathing, unless something prevents it, in order to purify the blood, and heal the belly around the third hour, as we have said; and take care that day of work, pain, luxury, and similar things; and be cheerful and joyful, and let the healer be higher than the one being healed, and stroke their arm two or three times, then loosen the band above moderately, for if it is too tight or too loose, the blood cannot flow; and then stroke the area with your hands until the veins fill up and can be felt; then moisten the healer's flame with a little old oil, then put their right hand on top of that belly below the navel one or two fingers where they want to heal, so that the belly does not fail and become inflamed.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, and si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, and ne puet ovrir li voinne, and ensi est on de ceus; and s'il avoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.

And if the vein opens up at first, that's good; if not, then try again a little below or above the same place in haste, unless the swelling does not appear.

And if the swelling is increased, and the patient becomes frightened, let him rest for a day or two, and do not bind the arm: by chance, an abscess may form there; nor should he enter the bath, then resume treatment if it pleases him; and if the wound is small, or the blood flows subtly, and you doubt that it will not bleed as much as you see, trust in that very same wound for all the bleeding straight away; and do some work hastily, as long as the swelling increases; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the swelling increase, do not continue the bleeding, and put a little bit of oil on top, for it lightens the body's blood, and is more nourishing in this swelling the oil; and thus administer the oil to each bleeding that you stop the veins, so as to stem the flow of blood; and it does the same trick and bowel movement, when one puts it on the swelling; and it thins out the liquid and spreads it when it becomes too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if a large abscess comes, which often happens, especially when it is not fully drained except at that time or the opening of the vein is small, then hurry and put a moist sponge on the swelling in water and warm oil for an hour; and you must do this after the bleeding from the vein has stopped, and if it remains at the site for some days with any blackness or greenish color, then it will not harm it; and if you see, put something of aloes or myrrh mixed with calamine, mustard, or similar.

Therefore do not put on any of what we have said, for by chance in short time the artery will burst; but make one dry plaster to harden the limb, then apply another dressing until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each blood according to its quantity and virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow until it becomes red; and if you see it thick, let it become thinner; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.

For there is a lot of blood inside the body that is already heated up, and it brings on fever; so one must draw out a great quantity, and enlarge the wound until it reaches its peak; then you reward all the conditions of the vein, and put your hand on the pulse when it is healthy, lest death come instead of healing, and this often happens when nurses are neglectful; and it does not matter when you see that the arm needs to be untied, and blood flows out for the second time, and the wound is closed, as long as you press strongly; or if it is curved, then quickly extend the arm, because this would be bad; but let it heal the second time; or you point to the tip of the flame, until the frozen blood that has congealed in the wound comes out, and put a poultice made from remade cloth in water on it, and press lightly.

Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein on the arm is healed at the site of the wound because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	Et the manner of healing is that the patient puts their hand in hot water until the fleshy part is red; then bind it moderately so that the vein appears well, then make the incision across, not along or lengthwise; and the punctures should be wide, and the bleeding should be good near the joint of the hand, and if there's no more to come out, put the hand in hot water again, and let the blood flow into the water until you have enough; and if it's winter, don't put the hand in hot water again, for it's put in more risk than in summer; and this incision is safer from all other incisions, as there are no arteries or nerves.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The healing of the saved part of the right hand is worth all liver diseases; and this is how it's done: strain the hand and put it in hot water until the vein is empty, so that one can see it; and if the wound bleeds across, and you take care to clean it completely, then nothing will be troubled; and don't go too far into the depth, for the nerves are under all denuded of flesh, and then put the hand back in hot water if the blood is congealed in the wound and can't come out.

Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The wound on the left hand side is worth as much to the disease of mice as it is to the illness of the right side; and does just as I told you there.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies. And the properties of its wound are that the patient douses his foot in hot water, and rubs it on the vein until it bleeds, and binds above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot there go many streams; then it cures either a larger stream or one at the ankle which is worth.

Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.
