And if a piece of bone projects forward and points downward below the knee, then do so above and below it, making the bone that we have said in the breaking of the forceps to soothe an abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	Of the breaking of the ribs.
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The weight is sometimes broken in mid-air, but this happens rarely; but it often breaks at the end.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in mid-air, so it falls below, and the patient feels great pain, and lacks strength, and all, and by chance vomits blood, and opens up the veins in the broken bone, and it seems to be well.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lies on their back, and one places a cushion between the shoulders, then presses the shoulders, and brings together the ribs of both sides with your hands, and subtly applies equal pressure in all the ways you can, until the shape of the bone is as it should be; then place poultices and bandages over the subtle layer of salt or other light material, and wrap it in one cloth, and tie it to the broken bone so that it does not move; and turn the cord around again on the back, and hold it fast, and reward every hour with a bind, and if it relapses, then bind it again; and if it needs to be removed due to corrosion or pruritus that comes from the site, or pain or abscess, then hasten, and remove it, and scrape off the poultice, and apply what has come forth in ways of cures; then reapply the poultice, and hold it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	Of the breaking of the ribs.
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the breaking of the ribs does not occur except in large people after the back and at the top inside, and they do not bend except because they are flabby; and one can tell well by examination of the back.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the restoration is that you set equal the break, as it is necessary.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply plaster, and bind with a strap, if you need to.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the breaking of the ribs is declining inwardly, then the patient feels very great pain and puncturing, as from pleurisy, for the bone pierces the membrane; and breathes in gasps, and all and vomits a great quantity of blood, and this is grave sickness, and the ancients have put great art into it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if there are those who say that one should administer foods that fill the belly to push the break backward.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do so, lest hot abscesses come there, if it has not already come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come, then let it heal.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And some of us say that one should place poultices on the site to suck strongly, and it seems reasonable; nevertheless, there is doubt whether the poultice will draw off the superfluidities from the site due to the weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some of us say that one should cover the site with wet wool in hot oil, and place tents between the ribs to put equal pressure on it, then be careful with the treatment of pleurisy, of meat and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot endure by the bone which points to the skin, and doubt is in the patient, then it is necessary to cut above the place of the broken rib, and it is necessary to put something below the instrument to guard against the sac; and then one must saw through the bone, and draw it out lightly, and then sew up the two lips of the wound, if they are large, and treat with plasters until he is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes forth, then put on wet cloths soaked in rose oil and place them over it; and cure the area around it as needed for the abscess, and be careful to apply it to the spot where it belongs, until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	Of the breaking of the neck.
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes the breaking occurs at the bone of the neck, and rarely does it bend; and similarly with the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if they will be healed or not, then take note if you see their hands softened and swollen and dead, and they cannot move or stretch them, and when you prick them with a needle, they do not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that he is mortal in many conditions, and if they are numb and feel well when they are strained and pricked, know that the joints of the bone are saved, and that the patient is healed, if one applies care.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if similar things happen to the spine of the back, and you want to know if it is healed or not, then take note if the feet are softened, and if there are swellings in the hands, and on the back there is a bursting forth and evacuation without desire; and when one has treated him on his belly, there is a bursting forth without desire.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he is oppressed on his back and wishes to rest, he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Know that it is mortal: if he does not labor greatly in his care.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if these accidents do not come to him, then the thing is easier.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is that you reward him if there is hot abscess, by applying rose oil or egg yolk oil to the spine, until it is calmed; then apply a poultice that comforts and dries, and bind it with a cloth, and instruct the patient to rest; and do not let them sleep on that part where they feel the pain, until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if some bones become loose, it is necessary to cover on the knee; and take out the bone, then bring together the two lips of the wound, if it is large, with a suture, then treat with ointment releasing fat, until he is healed. And if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the "head of the cow", then put your pouch in your left hand and place it evenly on top of the other hand at your power, then apply the poultice and cloth as needed; then bind it, and if there are loose bones, do so, and take out the bone, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	Of the breaking of the hipbone.
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	Rarely does the hipbone break, and if it does, it is not much diminished at the top; and it becomes long, and inclines downward, and comes to the patient's pain, and puncturing, and swelling up what breaks.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the treatment is that you stretch out your hand so far as to be above the breaking point; and know what kind of break it is and its shape; and if the break is only at the top, then place it in that same position until it is back to its natural figure.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is of great length or it declines inwardly, then cause the patient to lie on his belly until the restoration of that break is accomplished.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have put it straight, then place on the poultice, next a piece of wood or horn, and hold the break steady so that it does not move; and apply the hand below the ribs, until the breathing is equal.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on his healthy side or back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if the abscess comes forth, do not touch it, until the abscess has subsided and put on what we have said before; and then return to the restoration, and hold it as it should be, if there is no bad accident; and that's the way.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the break of the shoulder.
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder is that which is between the back and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, then it must be restored according to one of two ways: of which one is that you take a piece of wood as smooth as honey, in this shape:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two ends with two strings, and bend them upwards, and cause the patient to sit on a stool; then throw his broken arm onto the wood, until it comes into place, and has in middle a piece of wood, then bend on some heavy thing or let the attendants stretch it downwards; then put the break even with their hands together, until the break returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie. And if the bandage is near the top of the shoulder, it is necessary that you put the linen in the middle under the armpit, and the other one against the edge, under the bandage; and similarly if the bandage is on the edge, it is necessary to put the linen lightly, without labor, until the bandage is even on top and on the edge; then apply the same pressure, as needed, and restrain it, lest apostemes come there.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if abscesses come forth, then do not hold it at all until the 7th day, and put a moist cloth on it in a warm place and with rose oil, until the abscess is subsided; then hold it, and the manner of holding it is that you put the poultice on the break, then bring the arm onto the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or on the breast; and put the wrapping, and hold on the shoulder, and on the arm, so that the arm is in its natural state, unless something prevents it, or if the bone is not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone does not move, then use splints, and put on the break a larger and stronger splint than the others, with two spacers between each splint, and have each splint be so large that it passes over the break three spaces to either side; then hold on the splints, as I said at the beginning of this chapter on the break, more firmly and less far apart.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the settling of swelling and constriction as we have said, in the wound that you restore to the broken member, and you doubt the abscess is hot, let it remain attached until the seventh day, as we have said; then look at each one every three days, lest the swelling or inflammation come to the place, or the numbness cannot reach the member because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If it addresses, as we have said.

And if no such accident occurs, do not remove the binding until after three days or more, and have the patient lie on his back with his hands on his stomach; and place under the aid one cushion made of equal wool, and look each hour throughout the day or night to see that the shape of the broken member does not change or be softened by the bonds; if it addresses through the virtue of medicine, and give him food as we have put forward in such a way that the food is for the first subtlest; and when he begins to regain, let it be great.

de la brisure du bras	of the break of the arm
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "fascicles", one of which is small and is the one that follows the pouch; and the other is large and is the one that is below, towards the little toe. By chance, break only the large fascicle alone, or the small one, and by chance, both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When small bones are broken, the restoration is easy and the healing; and when great bones are broken, then the healing is poor, and more grievous than when they are both broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is only a small bone that is broken, then one must stretch and extend it slightly, and set it equal.

And if it is the great bone that is broken, then one must strain more strongly; and extend it on one cushion, and take hold of the little pouch with one's hand higher than the others, and the small bones lower than the others, and have the patient cross-legged over himself, with one cushion in front of him higher than the patient does not suffer any labor; then stretch the attendants' arms to the part below his hand or to the tie, and another attendant on the other above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then set the mirror equal, according to its best form.

Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the member and the ligament after some days.
